Essential AWS Services for Django, DevOps & Cloud Developers

40+ Services
Django DevOps Focus
Features

Comprehensive AWS services reference with practical examples and best practices: EC2, S3, Lambda, RDS, DynamoDB — featuring real-world scenarios and implementation guides for cloud architecture and development.

AWS Cloud DevOps Integration Infrastructure as Code Production Ready Best Practices

📑 Table of Contents

Essential AWS Services for Django, DevOps & Cloud Developers
Navigate through curated AWS services organized by category. Each service includes practical examples, best practices, and Django integration guides.

⚡ Compute

Virtual servers, serverless functions, and containers

  • Amazon EC2 - Virtual servers for hosting applications
  • AWS Lambda - Serverless functions for event-driven code
  • AWS Elastic Beanstalk - Easy application deployment and management
  • AWS Fargate - Serverless containers

💾 Storage

Object storage, block storage, and file systems

  • Amazon S3 - Object storage for static files, media, backups
  • Amazon EBS - Block storage for EC2 instances
  • Amazon EFS - Shared file system for multiple instances

🗄️ Database

Relational, NoSQL, and caching solutions

  • Amazon RDS - Managed PostgreSQL/MySQL for Django
  • Amazon Aurora - High-performance PostgreSQL/MySQL compatible
  • Amazon DynamoDB - NoSQL for high-scale applications
  • Amazon ElastiCache - Redis/Memcached for caching

🌐 Networking & CDN

VPC, load balancing, DNS, and content delivery

  • Amazon VPC - Virtual private network for resources
  • Elastic Load Balancing (ALB/NLB) - Distribute traffic across instances
  • Route 53 - DNS management and domain routing
  • AWS CloudFront - CDN for static assets and faster content delivery

🛠️ Developer Tools

CI/CD automation and code deployment

  • AWS CodePipeline - CI/CD automation
  • AWS CodeBuild - Build and test code
  • AWS CodeDeploy - Automated deployments
  • AWS CodeCommit - Git repository hosting

⚙️ Management & Governance

Monitoring, IaC, and server management

  • AWS CloudWatch - Monitoring, logs, and alerts
  • AWS CloudFormation - Infrastructure as Code (IaC)
  • AWS Systems Manager - Server management and automation
  • AWS CloudTrail - Audit logs and API tracking

🐳 Container Services

Container orchestration and registry

  • Amazon ECS - Container orchestration
  • Amazon EKS - Managed Kubernetes
  • Amazon ECR - Container image registry

🔒 Security & Identity

IAM, authentication, secrets, and encryption

  • AWS IAM - User and permission management
  • AWS Cognito - User authentication for applications
  • AWS Certificate Manager (ACM) - Free SSL/TLS certificates
  • AWS Secrets Manager - Store database credentials and API keys
  • AWS KMS - Encryption key management

🔗 Application Integration

Messaging, APIs, and workflow orchestration

  • Amazon SQS - Message queuing for async tasks
  • Amazon SNS - Push notifications and pub/sub messaging
  • Amazon API Gateway - Create and manage REST/GraphQL APIs
  • AWS Step Functions - Workflow orchestration

📊 Analytics & Monitoring

Log analysis, tracing, and data queries

  • Amazon CloudWatch Logs Insights - Query and analyze logs
  • AWS X-Ray - Distributed tracing and debugging
  • Amazon Athena - SQL queries on S3 data

💾 Backup & DR

Centralized backups and archival storage

  • AWS Backup - Centralized backup management
  • Amazon S3 Glacier - Long-term archival storage

🚀 Quick Reference

Django stack templates and DevOps guides

  • Typical Django Stack on AWS
  • Daily DevOps Tasks
  • Service Comparison Matrix
  • Cost Calculator Guide

Compute Services

AWS Compute Services provide scalable, secure, and reliable virtual computing resources for your Django applications. This section covers deploying and managing your anihpj job posting platform on AWS infrastructure.

Amazon EC2 (Elastic Compute Cloud)

Category: Compute  |  Use Case: Web Application Hosting  |  Pricing: On-Demand, Reserved, Spot Instances  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS EC2 Docs

Secure and resizable compute capacity in the cloud for hosting Django applications with automatic scaling, load balancing, and high availability.

📋 Overview & Introduction

Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud (EC2) is a web service that provides secure, resizable compute capacity in the cloud. It's designed to make web-scale cloud computing easier for developers by providing complete control over computing resources.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • Elastic Computing: Scale capacity up or down within minutes
  • Complete Control: Root access to instances and full control over computing resources
  • Flexible Pricing: Pay only for what you use with multiple pricing models
  • Integrated: Seamlessly works with other AWS services
  • Secure: Built-in firewall, VPC, and IAM integration
  • Reliable: 99.99% SLA with multiple availability zones
💡 When to Use EC2: Perfect for your anihpj Django job portal when you need full control over the server environment, custom configurations, or need to run background tasks, scheduled jobs, or WebSocket connections alongside your web application.
⚖️ EC2 vs. Other Compute Services
EC2: Full control, persistent, traditional apps
Lambda: Serverless, event-driven, short tasks
ECS/EKS: Container orchestration
Elastic Beanstalk: Managed platform for web apps
Lightsail: Simplified VPS for simple apps
Fargate: Serverless containers
🏗️ EC2 in AWS Ecosystem - Architecture Overview

│                        AWS CLOUD ECOSYSTEM                           │
│                                                                      │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │                    AMAZON VPC (Virtual Private Cloud)           │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │
│  │  │              Availability Zone A                          │  │ │
│  │  │                                                           │  │ │
│  │  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   EC2 Instance (anihpj-web-server-1)            │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   ┌─────────────────────────────────────┐       │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   │  Django Application                 │       │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   │  - JobPost Models                   │       │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   │  - Skills, Author, Location         │       │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   │  - Gunicorn WSGI Server             │       │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   └─────────────────────────────────────┘       │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │                                                  │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   Security Group: anihpj-sg                     │     │  │ │

│  │  │  │   - Port 80 (HTTP)                              │     │  │ │

│  │  │                          │                                │  │ │
│  │  │                          ├─→ EBS Volume (Root)            │  │ │

│  │                                                                 │ │

│  │  │              Availability Zone B                          │  │ │

│  │  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   EC2 Instance (anihpj-web-server-2)            │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │   (Mirror of Instance 1 for HA)                 │     │  │ │
│  │  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │  │ │
│  │  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │

🔧 Core Concepts

🖥️ EC2 Instances

An EC2 instance is a virtual server in Amazon's cloud. Think of it as a computer that you can configure and control, running your anihpj Django application.

📊 Instance Lifecycle States
┌─────────┐
│ Pending │  ← Launch initiated, instance is being prepared
└────┬────┘
     │
     ▼
┌─────────┐
│ Running │  ← Instance is running and you can connect to it
└────┬────┘     Your Django app is serving traffic here!
     │
     ├──→ [Reboot] ──→ Returns to Running
     │
     ▼
┌──────────┐
│ Stopping │  ← Stop command issued, instance is shutting down
└────┬─────┘
     │
     ▼
┌─────────┐
│ Stopped │  ← Instance is stopped (not charged for compute)
└────┬────┘     Still charged for EBS storage
     │
     ├──→ [Start] ──→ Returns to Pending → Running
     │
     ▼
┌─────────────┐
│ Terminating │  ← Delete command issued
└──────┬──────┘
       │
       ▼
┌────────────┐
│ Terminated │  ← Instance deleted permanently (can't recover)
└────────────┘
🏷️ Instance Types

EC2 offers different instance types optimized for various use cases. For your Django job portal, you'll typically use General Purpose instances.

📋 Instance Type Families
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    INSTANCE TYPE FAMILIES                         │
├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                   │
│  T Family (Burstable Performance)                                │
│  ├─ t3.micro, t3.small, t3.medium                                │
│  └─ 💡 Best for: Development, testing, low-traffic websites      │
│     ✅ Perfect for: Starting your anihpj portal                   │
│                                                                   │
│  M Family (General Purpose - Balanced)                           │
│  ├─ m5.large, m5.xlarge, m5.2xlarge                              │
│  └─ 💡 Best for: Production web apps, small-to-medium databases  │
│     ✅ Ideal for: Production anihpj with moderate traffic         │
│                                                                   │
│  C Family (Compute Optimized)                                    │
│  ├─ c5.large, c5.xlarge, c5.2xlarge                              │
│  └─ 💡 Best for: CPU-intensive tasks, batch processing           │
│     ✅ Use for: Heavy background job processing                   │
│                                                                   │
│  R Family (Memory Optimized)                                     │
│  ├─ r5.large, r5.xlarge, r5.2xlarge                              │
│  └─ 💡 Best for: In-memory caching, large datasets               │
│     ✅ Use for: Redis/Memcached for Django sessions               │
│                                                                   │
│  I Family (Storage Optimized)                                    │
│  ├─ i3.large, i3.xlarge, i3.2xlarge                              │
│  └─ 💡 Best for: High I/O databases, data warehousing            │
│                                                                   │
│  P/G Family (Accelerated Computing - GPU)                        │
│  ├─ p3.2xlarge, g4dn.xlarge                                      │
│  └─ 💡 Best for: Machine learning, video rendering               │
│                                                                   │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🔍 Instance Naming Convention Explained
Example: m5.xlarge

┌─┬──┬──────┐
│m│5 │xlarge│
└┬┘└┬┘└──┬───┘
 │  │   └─→ Size: nano, micro, small, medium, large, xlarge, 2xlarge, etc.
 │  │       • xlarge = 4 vCPUs, 16 GiB RAM (for m5 family)
 │  │       • 2xlarge = 8 vCPUs, 32 GiB RAM
 │  │
 │  └─→ Generation: 5 (latest generation for m family)
 │       • Higher generation = better performance & newer features
 │       • Always prefer latest generation when available
 │
 └─→ Family: m (General Purpose, balanced compute/memory)
      • t = Burstable
      • m = General Purpose
      • c = Compute Optimized
      • r = Memory Optimized
      • i = Storage Optimized

For anihpj Django Portal:
• Development: t3.micro (1 vCPU, 1 GiB RAM) → $0.0104/hour
• Staging: t3.small (2 vCPUs, 2 GiB RAM) → $0.0208/hour  
• Production: m5.large (2 vCPUs, 8 GiB RAM) → $0.096/hour

💿 AMIs (Amazon Machine Images)

An AMI is a template that contains the software configuration (operating system, application server, and applications) required to launch your instance.

🖼️ AMI Types & Selection Process
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                     AMI TYPES FOR DJANGO                      │
├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                               │
│  1. AWS-Provided AMIs (Recommended)                          │
│     ├─ Amazon Linux 2023 (Latest)                            │
│     │  • Optimized for AWS, free tier eligible               │
│     │  • Includes AWS CLI and tools                          │
│     │  • ✅ Great for production anihpj                       │
│     │                                                         │
│     ├─ Ubuntu Server 22.04 LTS                               │
│     │  • Popular for Django development                      │
│     │  • Large community support                             │
│     │  • ✅ Best for Django familiarity                       │
│     │                                                         │
│     └─ Amazon Linux 2                                        │
│        • Stable, long-term support                           │
│        • Good for enterprise applications                    │
│                                                               │
│  2. Marketplace AMIs                                         │
│     ├─ Bitnami Django Stack                                  │
│     │  • Pre-configured Django environment                   │
│     │  • Includes PostgreSQL, Nginx, SSL                     │
│     │  • ⚡ Quick start for anihpj                            │
│     │                                                         │
│     └─ Various vendor solutions                              │
│        • May have licensing costs                            │
│                                                               │
│  3. Community AMIs                                           │
│     └─ Shared by other AWS users                             │
│        • Use with caution (verify source)                    │
│        • Free, but less support                              │
│                                                               │
│  4. Custom AMIs (Your Own)                                   │
│     └─ Create snapshot of configured anihpj instance         │
│        • Pre-installed Django, dependencies                  │
│        • Pre-configured settings                             │
│        • ✅ Perfect for scaling identical instances           │
│                                                               │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

AMI Selection Workflow for anihpj:

Step 1: Launch Instance
        ↓
Step 2: Choose AMI
        ├─→ Quick Start → Ubuntu 22.04 LTS
        ├─→ Marketplace → Search "Django"
        ├─→ Community → Search specific configs
        └─→ My AMIs → Your custom anihpj AMI
        ↓
Step 3: Instance Type Selection
        ↓
Step 4: Configure & Launch
🌍 Regions & Availability Zones

AWS infrastructure is distributed globally across Regions and Availability Zones for high availability and low latency.

🗺️ AWS Global Infrastructure for anihpj
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                  AWS GLOBAL INFRASTRUCTURE                      │
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  REGION: us-east-1 (N. Virginia) - Most services available     │
│  ├─ Availability Zone A (use1-az1)                             │
│  │  └─ Data Center 1, 2, 3                                     │
│  │     • anihpj-web-server-1 ← Place your Django app here      │
│  │     • Independent power, cooling, networking                │
│  │                                                              │
│  ├─ Availability Zone B (use1-az2)                             │
│  │  └─ Data Center 4, 5, 6                                     │
│  │     • anihpj-web-server-2 ← Failover instance here          │
│  │     • Physically separate from AZ-A                         │
│  │                                                              │
│  └─ Availability Zone C (use1-az3)                             │
│     └─ Data Center 7, 8, 9                                     │
│        • anihpj-web-server-3 ← Additional redundancy           │
│                                                                 │
│  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────     │
│                                                                 │
│  REGION: eu-west-1 (Ireland) - European users                  │
│  └─ Deploy here if serving European job seekers                │
│     • Lower latency for EU users                               │
│     • GDPR compliance considerations                           │
│                                                                 │
│  REGION: ap-southeast-1 (Singapore) - Asian users              │
│  └─ Deploy here for Asian market                               │
│                                                                 │
└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Latency Considerations:
• Same AZ: < 1ms
• Different AZ (same region): 1-2ms
• Different Region: 50-300ms (depends on distance)

For anihpj Job Portal:
✅ Multi-AZ Deployment: High availability within same region
✅ Multi-Region: Global reach for international job postings

🚀 Getting Started with EC2 for Django

📋 Prerequisites
Before You Begin:
  • ✅ AWS Account created (aws.amazon.com)
  • ✅ IAM user with EC2 permissions (or use root account temporarily)
  • ✅ AWS CLI installed (optional but recommended)
  • ✅ SSH client installed (Linux/Mac: built-in, Windows: PuTTY or Windows Terminal)
  • ✅ Your anihpj Django code ready in Git repository
🔐 Required IAM Permissions
{
  "Version": "2012-10-17",
  "Statement": [
    {
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [
        "ec2:RunInstances",
        "ec2:TerminateInstances",
        "ec2:StopInstances",
        "ec2:StartInstances",
        "ec2:RebootInstances",
        "ec2:DescribeInstances",
        "ec2:DescribeImages",
        "ec2:DescribeKeyPairs",
        "ec2:DescribeSecurityGroups",
        "ec2:CreateKeyPair",
        "ec2:CreateSecurityGroup",
        "ec2:AuthorizeSecurityGroupIngress",
        "ec2:CreateTags",
        "ec2:DescribeVolumes",
        "ec2:AttachVolume"
      ],
      "Resource": "*"
    }
  ]
}

Save this as anihpj-ec2-policy.json and attach to your IAM user

🎯 Launch Your First EC2 Instance (Step-by-Step)
Step 1: Navigate to EC2 Console
1. Sign in to AWS Console (https://console.aws.amazon.com)
2. Search for "EC2" in the services search bar
3. Click "EC2" to open the EC2 Dashboard
4. Click orange "Launch Instance" button

🔌 Connecting to Your EC2 Instance
Method 1: SSH Connection (Linux/Mac/Windows)
# 1. Set correct permissions on your key file
chmod 400 anihpj-keypair.pem

# 2. Get your instance public IP from EC2 console
# Example: 54.123.45.67

# 3. Connect using SSH
ssh -i "anihpj-keypair.pem" ubuntu@54.123.45.67

# First time connection will ask:
# "Are you sure you want to continue connecting (yes/no)?"
# Type: yes

# ✅ You should now see:
# ubuntu@ip-172-31-10-10:~$
Welcome to Ubuntu 22.04.3 LTS (GNU/Linux 6.2.0-1009-aws x86_64) Last login: Mon Nov 3 10:30:15 2025 from 203.0.113.10 ubuntu@ip-172-31-10-10:~$
Method 2: EC2 Instance Connect (Browser-based)
1. Go to EC2 Console → Instances
2. Select your instance (anihpj-django-production)
3. Click "Connect" button (top right)
4. Choose "EC2 Instance Connect" tab
5. Username: ubuntu
6. Click "Connect"

✅ Opens terminal in browser - no SSH client needed!

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  EC2 Instance Connect                       │
│  ┌───────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │ ubuntu@ip-172-31-10-10:~$            │  │
│  │                                       │  │
│  │                                       │  │
│  └───────────────────────────────────────┘  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────┘

💡 Great for quick access without SSH keys!
Method 3: AWS Systems Manager Session Manager (Most Secure)
# No SSH keys needed, all access logged!

# 1. Install SSM agent (usually pre-installed on AWS AMIs)
# 2. Attach IAM role with SSM permissions to EC2 instance
# 3. Install AWS CLI locally
pip install awscli

# 4. Configure AWS CLI
aws configure

# 5. Start session
aws ssm start-session --target i-0abc123def456789

# ✅ Secure connection without opening port 22!
# All commands logged to CloudWatch for audit
✅ Instance Running! Your EC2 instance is now ready. Next step: Deploy your anihpj Django application!

🔑 Key Features & Components

💾 Storage Options

EC2 provides multiple storage options for your Django application, each optimized for different use cases.

📊 Storage Types Comparison
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                     EC2 STORAGE OPTIONS                              │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                      │
│  1. EBS (Elastic Block Store) - Persistent Network Storage          │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Type        │ IOPS      │ Throughput  │ Use Case             │ │
│  ├──────────────┼───────────┼─────────────┼──────────────────────┤ │
│  │ gp3 (SSD)    │ 3K-16K    │ 125-1000MB/s│ ✅ General Purpose   │ │
│  │              │           │             │    Boot volumes      │ │
│  │              │           │             │    Django app files  │ │
│  │              │           │             │    Most cost-effect. │ │
│  ├──────────────┼───────────┼─────────────┼──────────────────────┤ │
│  │ gp2 (SSD)    │ 100-16K   │ Varies      │ Legacy, use gp3      │ │
│  ├──────────────┼───────────┼─────────────┼──────────────────────┤ │
│  │ io2 (SSD)    │ Up to 64K │ Up to 1GB/s │ High-performance DB  │ │
│  │              │           │             │ Mission-critical     │ │
│  ├──────────────┼───────────┼─────────────┼──────────────────────┤ │
│  │ st1 (HDD)    │ 500       │ Up to 500MB │ Big data, logs       │ │
│  │              │           │             │ Sequential access    │ │
│  ├──────────────┼───────────┼─────────────┼──────────────────────┤ │
│  │ sc1 (HDD)    │ 250       │ Up to 250MB │ Cold storage         │ │
│  │              │           │             │ Infrequent access    │ │
│  └──────────────┴───────────┴─────────────┴──────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                      │
│  EBS Features:                                                       │
│  ✅ Persistent (survives instance stop/start)                        │
│  ✅ Snapshots for backup                                             │
│  ✅ Encryption at rest                                               │
│  ✅ Can attach/detach from instances                                 │
│  ✅ Replicated within AZ                                             │
│                                                                      │
│  2. Instance Store - Ephemeral Local Storage                        │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  • Physically attached to host computer                        │ │
│  │  • Very high IOPS (millions)                                   │ │
│  │  • ⚠️ Data lost on instance stop/termination                    │ │
│  │  • Use for: Temporary cache, buffers, scratch data            │ │
│  │  • ❌ Don't use for: Django database, user uploads             │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                      │
│  3. EFS (Elastic File System) - Shared Network File System          │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  • Shared across multiple EC2 instances                        │ │
│  │  • Auto-scales (petabytes)                                     │ │
│  │  • Use for: Shared media uploads in anihpj                     │ │
│  │  • Multiple web servers accessing same files                   │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                      │
│  4. S3 Integration - Object Storage                                 │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  • Store Django static files (CSS, JS, images)                 │ │
│  │  • User uploaded files (resumes, company logos)                │ │
│  │  • Cheaper than EBS for large files                            │ │
│  │  • Use django-storages library                                 │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                      │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

For anihpj Job Portal:
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  Component              │ Storage Type            │
├─────────────────────────┼─────────────────────────┤
│  OS & Django app        │ EBS gp3 (20 GB)         │
│  Database (if local)    │ EBS gp3 (30 GB)         │
│  Static files (prod)    │ S3                      │
│  User uploads (resumes) │ S3                      │
│  Application logs       │ EBS + CloudWatch        │
│  Session cache          │ Redis on separate EBS   │
└────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
💿 Attaching Additional EBS Volume
# Create new EBS volume for Django media files
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --size 30 \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-media-storage}]'

# Output: vol-0abc123def456789

# Attach volume to instance
aws ec2 attach-volume \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123def456789 \
    --instance-id i-0abc123def456789 \
    --device /dev/sdf

# On the instance, format and mount
sudo mkfs -t ext4 /dev/xvdf
sudo mkdir /opt/anihpj/media
sudo mount /dev/xvdf /opt/anihpj/media

# Add to /etc/fstab for persistent mount
echo '/dev/xvdf /opt/anihpj/media ext4 defaults,nofail 0 2' | sudo tee -a /etc/fstab

# Update Django settings.py
# MEDIA_ROOT = '/opt/anihpj/media/'

🔌 VPC Integration Architecture
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    VPC (Virtual Private Cloud)                   │
│                    CIDR: 10.0.0.0/16                             │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                  │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  PUBLIC SUBNET (10.0.1.0/24) - AZ-A                        │ │
│  │  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │
│  │  │  EC2: anihpj-web-1                                   │  │ │
│  │  │  Private IP: 10.0.1.10                               │  │ │
│  │  │  Public IP: 54.123.45.67 (Elastic IP)               │  │ │
│  │  │  └─ Django App + Nginx                               │  │ │
│  │  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  Internet Gateway ← Routes traffic to/from internet         │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  PRIVATE SUBNET (10.0.2.0/24) - AZ-A                       │ │
│  │  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │
│  │  │  RDS Database                                        │  │ │
│  │  │  Private IP: 10.0.2.20                               │  │ │
│  │  │  No public IP (more secure)                          │  │ │
│  │  │  └─ PostgreSQL for JobPost, Skills, Author, Location│  │ │
│  │  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  NAT Gateway ← Allows outbound internet (for updates)       │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  PUBLIC SUBNET (10.0.3.0/24) - AZ-B (High Availability)   │ │
│  │  └─ EC2: anihpj-web-2 (failover instance)                  │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Security Groups (Virtual Firewalls):
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  anihpj-web-sg (Applied to Web Servers)                         │
│  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │ Inbound Rules:                                            │  │
│  │  • SSH (22) from 203.0.113.0/24 (your office)            │  │
│  │  • HTTP (80) from 0.0.0.0/0 (anywhere)                   │  │
│  │  • HTTPS (443) from 0.0.0.0/0 (anywhere)                 │  │
│  ├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤  │
│  │ Outbound Rules:                                           │  │
│  │  • All traffic to 0.0.0.0/0 (default)                    │  │
│  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│                                                                  │
│  anihpj-db-sg (Applied to Database)                             │
│  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │ Inbound Rules:                                            │  │
│  │  • PostgreSQL (5432) from anihpj-web-sg only             │  │
│  │    (security group reference - more secure)              │  │
│  ├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤  │
│  │ Outbound Rules:                                           │  │
│  │  • None needed (database doesn't initiate connections)   │  │
│  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🔗 Elastic IP Address (Static IP)
# Allocate Elastic IP
aws ec2 allocate-address --domain vpc

# Output:
# {
#     "PublicIp": "54.123.45.67",
#     "AllocationId": "eipalloc-0abc123",
#     "Domain": "vpc"
# }

# Associate with your instance
aws ec2 associate-address \
    --instance-id i-0abc123def456789 \
    --allocation-id eipalloc-0abc123

# Benefits for anihpj:
# ✅ IP persists even if instance is stopped/started
# ✅ Can quickly reassign to failover instance
# ✅ Use in DNS records (A record for anihpj.com)
# ✅ Simpler firewall rules
💡 Elastic IP for Production: Always use Elastic IP for production Django apps so your DNS doesn't break when you restart instances. First 1 Elastic IP per running instance is free!
🎯 Placement Groups
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                 PLACEMENT GROUP STRATEGIES                │
├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                           │
│  1. Cluster Placement Group                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Same Rack / Same AZ                                │ │
│  │  ┌────┐ ┌────┐ ┌────┐ ┌────┐                       │ │
│  │  │EC2 │ │EC2 │ │EC2 │ │EC2 │                       │ │
│  │  │ 1  │ │ 2  │ │ 3  │ │ 4  │                       │ │
│  │  └────┘ └────┘ └────┘ └────┘                       │ │
│  │  ✅ Low latency (microseconds)                       │ │
│  │  ✅ High network throughput (10 Gbps)               │ │
│  │  ❌ Single point of failure                         │ │
│  │  Use for: HPC, big data processing                 │ │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                           │
│  2. Spread Placement Group                               │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Different Racks / Multiple AZs                     │ │
│  │  Rack 1    Rack 2    Rack 3    Rack 4              │ │
│  │  ┌────┐   ┌────┐   ┌────┐   ┌────┐               │ │
│  │  │EC2 │   │EC2 │   │EC2 │   │EC2 │               │ │
│  │  │ 1  │   │ 2  │   │ 3  │   │ 4  │               │ │
│  │  └────┘   └────┘   └────┘   └────┘               │ │
│  │  ✅ High availability                                │ │
│  │  ✅ Fault tolerance                                  │ │
│  │  ✅ Max 7 instances per AZ                           │ │
│  │  Use for: Critical anihpj production servers       │ │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                           │
│  3. Partition Placement Group                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Partitions with multiple instances                 │ │
│  │  Part-1      Part-2      Part-3                     │ │
│  │  ┌──────┐   ┌──────┐   ┌──────┐                    │ │
│  │  │ EC2  │   │ EC2  │   │ EC2  │                    │ │
│  │  │ EC2  │   │ EC2  │   │ EC2  │                    │ │
│  │  └──────┘   └──────┘   └──────┘                    │ │
│  │  ✅ Up to 7 partitions per AZ                        │ │
│  │  ✅ Reduces correlated failures                      │ │
│  │  Use for: Distributed systems (Kafka, Hadoop)      │ │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                           │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

For anihpj: Use Spread Placement Group for production servers
🔒 Security Features
🛡️ Security Groups vs Network ACLs
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         SECURITY GROUPS vs NETWORK ACLs                          │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                  │
│  Security Groups (Instance-level Firewall)                      │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  • STATEFUL (return traffic auto-allowed)                  │ │
│  │  • Applied to ENI (Elastic Network Interface)              │ │
│  │  • Only ALLOW rules (no deny)                              │ │
│  │  • All rules evaluated                                     │ │
│  │                                                             │ │
│  │  Example for anihpj-web-sg:                                │ │
│  │  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │
│  │  │ Inbound:                                             │  │ │
│  │  │  Rule 1: Allow SSH (22) from 203.0.113.0/24         │  │ │
│  │  │  Rule 2: Allow HTTP (80) from 0.0.0.0/0             │  │ │
│  │  │  Rule 3: Allow HTTPS (443) from 0.0.0.0/0           │  │ │
│  │  │                                                       │  │ │
│  │  │ Outbound:                                            │  │ │
│  │  │  Rule 1: Allow all traffic to 0.0.0.0/0             │  │ │
│  │  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Network ACLs (Subnet-level Firewall)                           │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  • STATELESS (must allow return traffic explicitly)        │ │
│  │  • Applied to entire subnet                                │ │
│  │  • Both ALLOW and DENY rules                               │ │
│  │  • Rules evaluated in order (lowest number first)          │ │
│  │                                                             │ │
│  │  Example for anihpj public subnet:                         │ │
│  │  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │
│  │  │ Inbound:                                             │  │ │
│  │  │  100: Allow HTTP (80) from 0.0.0.0/0                 │  │ │
│  │  │  110: Allow HTTPS (443) from 0.0.0.0/0               │  │ │
│  │  │  120: Allow SSH (22) from 203.0.113.0/24             │  │ │
│  │  │  130: Allow Ephemeral ports (1024-65535)             │  │ │
│  │  │  *  : Deny all (implicit)                            │  │ │
│  │  │                                                       │  │ │
│  │  │ Outbound:                                            │  │ │
│  │  │  100: Allow HTTP (80) to 0.0.0.0/0                   │  │ │
│  │  │  110: Allow HTTPS (443) to 0.0.0.0/0                 │  │ │
│  │  │  120: Allow Ephemeral ports (1024-65535)             │  │ │
│  │  │  *  : Deny all (implicit)                            │  │ │
│  │  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Best Practice for anihpj:                                 │ │
│  │  1. Use Security Groups as primary defense                 │ │
│  │  2. Use Network ACLs for additional subnet-level rules     │ │
│  │  3. Deny known malicious IPs at NACL level                 │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🔑 IAM Roles for EC2
// Create IAM role for anihpj EC2 instances
{
  "Version": "2012-10-17",
  "Statement": [
    {
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [
        "s3:GetObject",
        "s3:PutObject",
        "s3:DeleteObject",
        "s3:ListBucket"
      ],
      "Resource": [
        "arn:aws:s3:::anihpj-static-files/*",
        "arn:aws:s3:::anihpj-media-uploads/*"
      ]
    },
    {
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [
        "rds:DescribeDBInstances",
        "rds:Connect"
      ],
      "Resource": "arn:aws:rds:us-east-1:123456789012:db:anihpj-db"
    },
    {
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [
        "cloudwatch:PutMetricData",
        "logs:CreateLogGroup",
        "logs:CreateLogStream",
        "logs:PutLogEvents"
      ],
      "Resource": "*"
    },
    {
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [
        "ses:SendEmail",
        "ses:SendRawEmail"
      ],
      "Resource": "*",
      "Condition": {
        "StringEquals": {
          "ses:FromAddress": "noreply@anihpj.com"
        }
      }
    }
  ]
}
# Create role
aws iam create-role \
    --role-name anihpj-ec2-role \
    --assume-role-policy-document file://trust-policy.json

# Attach policy
aws iam put-role-policy \
    --role-name anihpj-ec2-role \
    --policy-name anihpj-permissions \
    --policy-document file://permissions.json

# Create instance profile
aws iam create-instance-profile \
    --instance-profile-name anihpj-ec2-profile

# Add role to profile
aws iam add-role-to-instance-profile \
    --instance-profile-name anihpj-ec2-profile \
    --role-name anihpj-ec2-role

# Attach to EC2 instance
aws ec2 associate-iam-instance-profile \
    --instance-id i-0abc123def456789 \
    --iam-instance-profile Name=anihpj-ec2-profile
✅ Security Best Practice: Never store AWS credentials in your Django code! Always use IAM roles for EC2 instances to access other AWS services securely.
🔐 Encryption Options
# Enable EBS encryption by default in your account
aws ec2 enable-ebs-encryption-by-default

# Create encrypted EBS volume
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --size 30 \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --encrypted \
    --kms-key-id arn:aws:kms:us-east-1:123456789012:key/abcd1234 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-encrypted-data}]'

# Encryption features:
# ✅ Data encrypted at rest
# ✅ Data encrypted in transit (between EC2 and EBS)
# ✅ Snapshots automatically encrypted
# ✅ KMS key management for compliance
# ✅ No performance impact

# For Django: Encrypt volumes containing:
# • Database files
# • User uploaded data (resumes)
# • Application logs
# • Backup files

🚨 CloudWatch Alarms for anihpj
# Create CPU alarm
aws cloudwatch put-metric-alarm \
    --alarm-name anihpj-high-cpu \
    --alarm-description "Alert when CPU exceeds 80%" \
    --metric-name CPUUtilization \
    --namespace AWS/EC2 \
    --statistic Average \
    --period 300 \
    --threshold 80 \
    --comparison-operator GreaterThanThreshold \
    --evaluation-periods 2 \
    --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=i-0abc123def456789 \
    --alarm-actions arn:aws:sns:us-east-1:123456789012:anihpj-alerts

# Create disk alarm
aws cloudwatch put-metric-alarm \
    --alarm-name anihpj-low-disk-space \
    --alarm-description "Alert when disk usage exceeds 85%" \
    --metric-name disk_used_percent \
    --namespace CWAgent \
    --statistic Average \
    --period 300 \
    --threshold 85 \
    --comparison-operator GreaterThanThreshold \
    --evaluation-periods 1 \
    --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=i-0abc123def456789 \
    --alarm-actions arn:aws:sns:us-east-1:123456789012:anihpj-alerts

# Create memory alarm
aws cloudwatch put-metric-alarm \
    --alarm-name anihpj-high-memory \
    --alarm-description "Alert when memory exceeds 90%" \
    --metric-name mem_used_percent \
    --namespace CWAgent \
    --statistic Average \
    --period 300 \
    --threshold 90 \
    --comparison-operator GreaterThanThreshold \
    --evaluation-periods 2 \
    --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=i-0abc123def456789 \
    --alarm-actions arn:aws:sns:us-east-1:123456789012:anihpj-alerts

# Create status check alarm
aws cloudwatch put-metric-alarm \
    --alarm-name anihpj-instance-status-check \
    --alarm-description "Alert when instance status check fails" \
    --metric-name StatusCheckFailed_Instance \
    --namespace AWS/EC2 \
    --statistic Maximum \
    --period 60 \
    --threshold 0 \
    --comparison-operator GreaterThanThreshold \
    --evaluation-periods 2 \
    --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=i-0abc123def456789 \
    --alarm-actions arn:aws:sns:us-east-1:123456789012:anihpj-critical-alerts \
    --treat-missing-data notBreaching
📝 Custom Django Application Metrics
# anihpj/middleware/cloudwatch_metrics.py
import boto3
from django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin
from datetime import datetime

class CloudWatchMetricsMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):
    """Send custom Django metrics to CloudWatch"""
    
    def __init__(self, get_response):
        super().__init__(get_response)
        self.cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name='us-east-1')
    
    def process_response(self, request, response):
        # Track response times
        if hasattr(request, '_start_time'):
            response_time = (datetime.now() - request._start_time).total_seconds()
            
            self.cloudwatch.put_metric_data(
                Namespace='AnihpjJobPortal',
                MetricData=[
                    {
                        'MetricName': 'ResponseTime',
                        'Value': response_time,
                        'Unit': 'Seconds',
                        'Dimensions': [
                            {'Name': 'View', 'Value': request.path},
                            {'Name': 'Method', 'Value': request.method}
                        ]
                    }
                ]
            )
        
        # Track HTTP status codes
        self.cloudwatch.put_metric_data(
            Namespace='AnihpjJobPortal',
            MetricData=[
                {
                    'MetricName': 'HTTPStatusCode',
                    'Value': 1,
                    'Unit': 'Count',
                    'Dimensions': [
                        {'Name': 'StatusCode', 'Value': str(response.status_code)},
                        {'Name': 'Path', 'Value': request.path}
                    ]
                }
            ]
        )
        
        return response
    
    def process_request(self, request):
        request._start_time = datetime.now()


# Track custom business metrics
def track_job_post_created(job_post):
    """Track when new job is posted"""
    cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch')
    cloudwatch.put_metric_data(
        Namespace='AnihpjJobPortal',
        MetricData=[
            {
                'MetricName': 'JobPostsCreated',
                'Value': 1,
                'Unit': 'Count',
                'Dimensions': [
                    {'Name': 'Company', 'Value': job_post.author.company},
                    {'Name': 'JobType', 'Value': job_post.type}
                ]
            }
        ]
    )

def track_job_application(job_post):
    """Track when someone applies to a job"""
    cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch')
    cloudwatch.put_metric_data(
        Namespace='AnihpjJobPortal',
        MetricData=[
            {
                'MetricName': 'JobApplications',
                'Value': 1,
                'Unit': 'Count',
                'Dimensions': [
                    {'Name': 'JobTitle', 'Value': job_post.title},
                    {'Name': 'Location', 'Value': job_post.location.city}
                ]
            }
        ]
    )

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    EC2 PRICING MODELS                                │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                      │
│  1. ON-DEMAND (Pay-per-second, no commitment)                       │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Instance Type │ On-Demand Price │ Monthly (730 hrs)          │ │
│  ├────────────────┼─────────────────┼────────────────────────────┤ │
│  │  t3.micro      │ $0.0104/hour    │ $7.59/month               │ │
│  │  t3.small      │ $0.0208/hour    │ $15.18/month              │ │
│  │  t3.medium     │ $0.0416/hour    │ $30.37/month              │ │
│  │  m5.large      │ $0.096/hour     │ $70.08/month              │ │
│  │  m5.xlarge     │ $0.192/hour     │ $140.16/month             │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  ✅ No upfront payment                                          │ │
│  │  ✅ Pay only for running instances                              │ │
│  │  ✅ Flexible - start/stop anytime                               │ │
│  │  ❌ Most expensive option                                       │ │
│  │  Use for: Development, testing, unpredictable workloads        │ │

│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  ✅ Significant cost savings (38-72%)                           │ │
│  │  ✅ Capacity reservation                                        │ │

│  │  ❌ Commitment required                                         │ │

│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Commit to $10/hour for 1 year = Save 40-72%                  │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  Types:                                                         │ │
│  │  • Compute Savings Plans (most flexible)                       │ │
│  │    - Any instance type, region, OS                             │ │
│  │    - Up to 66% savings                                         │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  • EC2 Instance Savings Plans                                  │ │
│  │    - Specific instance family (e.g., m5)                       │ │
│  │    - Up to 72% savings                                         │ │
│  │    - Can change size (m5.large → m5.xlarge)                    │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  ✅ More flexible than Reserved Instances                       │ │
│  │  ✅ Auto-applies to matching usage                              │ │
│  │  Use for: Stable production workloads                          │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                      │
│  4. SPOT INSTANCES (Unused capacity, up to 90% savings)             │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  m5.large Spot: $0.0288/hour (70% cheaper!)                   │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  How it works:                                                 │ │
│  │  1. Set max price you're willing to pay                       │ │
│  │  2. Get instance when spot price < max price                  │ │
│  │  3. AWS can terminate with 2-minute warning                   │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  ✅ Massive savings (50-90%)                                    │ │
│  │  ✅ Good for flexible, fault-tolerant workloads                 │ │
│  │  ❌ Can be interrupted                                          │ │
│  │  ❌ Not recommended for production web servers                  │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  Use for anihpj:                                               │ │
│  │  • Batch processing (email notifications)                     │ │
│  │  • Data analysis (job market trends)                          │ │
│  │  • Testing/staging environments                               │ │
│  │  • Background job workers                                     │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                      │
│  5. DEDICATED HOSTS (Physical server for compliance)                │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  m5.large Dedicated Host: $1,642.80/month                      │ │
│  │  (Can run multiple instances on same physical server)          │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  ✅ Compliance requirements (bring-your-own-license)            │ │
│  │  ✅ Visibility into sockets, cores, host ID                     │ │
│  │  ❌ Most expensive option                                       │ │
│  │  Use for: Enterprise compliance needs only                     │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                      │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

RECOMMENDATION FOR ANIHPJ:
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
Development:     t3.micro On-Demand      →  $7.59/month
Staging:         t3.small On-Demand      →  $15.18/month  
Production:      m5.large Reserved (1yr) →  $43.22/month (save $27)
Background Jobs: m5.large Spot           →  $21.02/month (save $49)

Total Monthly: ~$87/month vs $133 On-Demand (35% savings!)
💡 Cost Optimization Strategies for anihpj
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│            COST OPTIMIZATION CHECKLIST                           │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                  │
│  1. Right-Sizing                                                │
│  ☑ Monitor CPU, memory, network usage for 2+ weeks              │
│  ☑ Use AWS Compute Optimizer recommendations                    │
│  ☑ Start small (t3.micro) and scale up as needed                │
│  ☑ Review monthly and adjust instance types                     │
│                                                                  │
│  Example: anihpj running at 20% CPU on m5.large                 │
│  → Downgrade to t3.medium                                       │
│  → Save $39.71/month (56% reduction!)                           │
│                                                                  │
│  2. Stop Non-Production Instances                               │
│  ☑ Stop dev/test instances nights & weekends                    │
│  ☑ Use scheduled actions (Lambda + EventBridge)                 │
│  ☑ Tag instances: AutoStop=true                                 │
│                                                                  │
│  Example: Stop dev instance 16 hours/day + weekends             │
│  → Running only 8 hrs/day × 5 days = 40 hrs/week                │
│  → vs 168 hrs/week = Save 76%!                                  │
│  → t3.micro: $7.59/month → $1.82/month                          │
│                                                                  │
│  3. Use Reserved Instances for Production                       │
│  ☑ 1-year commitment for stable production workloads             │
│  ☑ Mix of 1-year and 3-year for predictable savings             │
│  ☑ Start with No Upfront if cash-constrained                    │
│                                                                  │
│  4. Leverage Spot Instances                                     │
│  ☑ Use for batch jobs (sending job alert emails)                │
│  ☑ Use for CI/CD pipelines                                      │
│  ☑ Use for data processing (analytics)                          │
│  ☑ Set max price to avoid surprises                             │
│                                                                  │
│  5. Optimize Storage                                            │
│  ☑ Use gp3 instead of gp2 (20% cheaper)                          │
│  ☑ Delete old EBS snapshots (automate with lifecycle)           │
│  ☑ Move static files to S3 ($0.023/GB vs $0.10/GB for EBS)     │
│  ☑ Use S3 Intelligent-Tiering for uploads                       │
│                                                                  │
│  Example: 100 GB of static files                                │
│  → EBS gp3: $8/month                                            │
│  → S3 Standard: $2.30/month                                     │
│  → Save $5.70/month (71% reduction!)                            │
│                                                                  │
│  6. Use Auto Scaling                                            │
│  ☑ Scale down during low traffic periods                        │
│  ☑ Scale up during peak hours                                   │
│  ☑ Min: 1 instance, Max: 4 instances                            │
│                                                                  │
│  Example: Auto scale anihpj                                     │
│  → 1 instance off-peak (20 hrs/day)                             │
│  → 3 instances peak (4 hrs/day)                                 │
│  → Average: 1.33 instances vs 3 always-on                       │
│  → Save 55% on compute costs!                                   │
│                                                                  │
│  7. Implement Caching                                           │
│  ☑ Use ElastiCache (Redis) for sessions                         │
│  ☑ Cache database queries                                       │
│  ☑ Use CloudFront CDN for static assets                         │
│  ☑ Reduce EC2 instance size needs                               │
│                                                                  │
│  8. Monitor and Alert                                           │
│  ☑ Set up AWS Budgets ($50/month alert)                         │
│  ☑ Enable Cost Anomaly Detection                                │
│  ☑ Review Cost Explorer monthly                                 │
│  ☑ Tag all resources for cost allocation                        │
│                                                                  │
│  9. Use Cost Allocation Tags                                    │
│  ☑ Tag: Environment=production/staging/dev                      │
│  ☑ Tag: Project=anihpj                                          │
│  ☑ Tag: Team=engineering                                        │
│  ☑ Tag: CostCenter=product-development                          │
│                                                                  │
│  10. Optimize Data Transfer                                     │
│  ☑ Use VPC endpoints for S3 (no data transfer charges)          │
│  ☑ Keep data in same region                                     │
│  ☑ Use CloudFront for international users                       │
│                                                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

💾 EBS Volume Type Comparison
Filter by Use Case:
Volume Type Storage Class Max IOPS Max Throughput Price per GB/month Best For Use Case
gp3 SSD 16,000 1,000 MB/s $0.08 ⭐ Most workloads Django apps, databases, boot volumes
gp2 SSD 16,000 250 MB/s $0.10 Legacy workloads Older applications (use gp3 instead)
io2 Provisioned IOPS SSD 64,000 1,000 MB/s $0.125 + IOPS cost Mission-critical Large databases, high-traffic apps
io2 Block Express Provisioned IOPS SSD 256,000 4,000 MB/s $0.125 + IOPS cost Extreme performance SAP HANA, large Oracle databases
st1 Throughput Optimized HDD 500 500 MB/s $0.045 Big data, logs Data warehouses, log processing
sc1 Cold HDD 250 250 MB/s $0.015 Infrequent access Backups, archives (lowest cost)

💡 Recommendation for Django Job Portal: Use gp3 for root volumes (20 GB) and application data. It's 20% cheaper than gp2 with better performance. For backups, consider sc1 for maximum cost savings.

│         │               │               │                       │

│  │ AZ-A       │  │ AZ-B       │  │ AZ-C       │              │
│  │            │  │            │  │            │              │

│  Auto Scaling Group: anihpj-asg                                 │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │

│  │                                                             │ │

│  │  Health Check Grace Period: 300 seconds                    │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Scaling Triggers:                                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  📈 SCALE OUT (Add instances)                               │ │
│  │  • CPU > 70% for 5 minutes  → Add 1 instance               │ │
│  │  • Memory > 80% for 5 min   → Add 1 instance               │ │
│  │  • Active connections > 1000 → Add 1 instance               │ │
│  │  • Scheduled: 8am weekdays  → Add 2 instances               │ │
│  │                                                             │ │
│  │  📉 SCALE IN (Remove instances)                             │ │
│  │  • CPU < 30% for 10 minutes → Remove 1 instance            │ │
│  │  • After business hours     → Remove 2 instances           │ │
│  │  • Weekends (low traffic)   → Scale to minimum             │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Benefits:                                                       │
│  ✅ Handle traffic spikes automatically                          │
│  ✅ Reduce costs during low-traffic periods                      │
│  ✅ Maintain performance and availability                        │
│  ✅ No manual intervention needed                                │
│                                                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

# Create launch template for anihpj
aws ec2 create-launch-template \
    --launch-template-name anihpj-launch-template \
    --launch-template-data '{
        "ImageId": "ami-0c7217cdde317cfec",
        "InstanceType": "m5.large",
        "KeyName": "anihpj-keypair",
        "IamInstanceProfile": {
            "Name": "anihpj-ec2-profile"
        },
        "SecurityGroupIds": ["sg-0abc123def456789"],
        "UserData": "'$(base64 -w 0 user-data.sh)'",
        "BlockDeviceMappings": [
            {
                "DeviceName": "/dev/sda1",
                "Ebs": {
                    "VolumeSize": 20,
                    "VolumeType": "gp3",
                    "DeleteOnTermination": true,
                    "Encrypted": true
                }
            }
        ],
        "TagSpecifications": [
            {
                "ResourceType": "instance",
                "Tags": [
                    {"Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-auto-scaled"},
                    {"Key": "Project", "Value": "anihpj"},
                    {"Key": "Environment", "Value": "production"},
                    {"Key": "ManagedBy", "Value": "AutoScaling"}
                ]
            }
        ],
        "Monitoring": {
            "Enabled": true
        }
    }'
⚙️ Create Auto Scaling Group
# Create Auto Scaling Group
aws autoscaling create-auto-scaling-group \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --launch-template LaunchTemplateName=anihpj-launch-template,Version='$Latest' \
    --min-size 1 \
    --max-size 6 \
    --desired-capacity 2 \
    --default-cooldown 300 \
    --health-check-type ELB \
    --health-check-grace-period 300 \
    --vpc-zone-identifier "subnet-0abc123,subnet-0def456,subnet-0ghi789" \
    --target-group-arns "arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:targetgroup/anihpj-tg/abc123" \
    --tags "Key=Name,Value=anihpj-asg-instance,PropagateAtLaunch=true" \
           "Key=Environment,Value=production,PropagateAtLaunch=true"

# Create scaling policies

# 1. Target Tracking Scaling (Recommended - Simple!)
aws autoscaling put-scaling-policy \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --policy-name anihpj-target-tracking-cpu \
    --policy-type TargetTrackingScaling \
    --target-tracking-configuration '{
        "PredefinedMetricSpecification": {
            "PredefinedMetricType": "ASGAverageCPUUtilization"
        },
        "TargetValue": 70.0
    }'

# 2. Step Scaling Policy (More control)
aws autoscaling put-scaling-policy \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --policy-name anihpj-scale-out-policy \
    --policy-type StepScaling \
    --adjustment-type ChangeInCapacity \
    --metric-aggregation-type Average \
    --step-adjustments \
        MetricIntervalLowerBound=0,MetricIntervalUpperBound=10,ScalingAdjustment=1 \
        MetricIntervalLowerBound=10,ScalingAdjustment=2

# 3. Scheduled Scaling (Predictable patterns)
# Scale up weekday mornings
aws autoscaling put-scheduled-update-group-action \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --scheduled-action-name anihpj-scale-up-morning \
    --recurrence "0 8 * * MON-FRI" \
    --desired-capacity 4

# Scale down weekday evenings
aws autoscaling put-scheduled-update-group-action \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --scheduled-action-name anihpj-scale-down-evening \
    --recurrence "0 18 * * MON-FRI" \
    --desired-capacity 2

# Scale to minimum on weekends
aws autoscaling put-scheduled-update-group-action \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --scheduled-action-name anihpj-weekend-minimum \
    --recurrence "0 0 * * SAT" \
    --desired-capacity 1
⚖️ Load Balancing
📊 Load Balancer Types Comparison
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│               ELASTIC LOAD BALANCER TYPES                        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                  │
│  1. APPLICATION LOAD BALANCER (ALB) - Layer 7 (HTTP/HTTPS)      │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  ✅ Best for: Django web applications (anihpj)              │ │
│  │  ✅ Path-based routing: /api/* → API servers                │ │
│  │  ✅ Host-based routing: api.anihpj.com vs www.anihpj.com    │ │
│  │  ✅ SSL/TLS termination                                      │ │
│  │  ✅ WebSocket support                                        │ │
│  │  ✅ HTTP/2 support                                           │ │
│  │  ✅ Authentication (OIDC, Cognito)                           │ │
│  │  ✅ Request/response headers modification                    │ │
│  │  ✅ Lambda targets support                                   │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  Price: $0.0225/hour + $0.008/LCU-hour                     │ │
│  │        (~$16.20/month + data processed)                     │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  Use Case: anihpj Django application ← RECOMMENDED          │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  2. NETWORK LOAD BALANCER (NLB) - Layer 4 (TCP/UDP)             │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  ✅ Ultra-low latency (microseconds)                         │ │
│  │  ✅ Millions of requests per second                          │ │
│  │  ✅ Static IP support                                        │ │
│  │  ✅ TCP, UDP, TLS protocols                                  │ │
│  │  ❌ No path-based routing                                    │ │
│  │  ❌ No HTTP header inspection                                │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  Use Case: Real-time gaming, IoT, high-performance apps    │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  3. CLASSIC LOAD BALANCER (CLB) - Legacy                        │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  ⚠️ Legacy, use ALB or NLB instead                           │ │
│  │  Layer 4 & 7, but fewer features                           │ │
│  │  Being phased out                                           │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  4. GATEWAY LOAD BALANCER (GWLB) - Layer 3                      │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  For virtual appliances (firewalls, IDS/IPS)               │ │
│  │  Not typically used for web applications                   │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🔧 Configure Application Load Balancer
# 1. Create Target Group
aws elbv2 create-target-group \
    --name anihpj-target-group \
    --protocol HTTP \
    --port 80 \
    --vpc-id vpc-0abc123 \
    --health-check-enabled \
    --health-check-path /health/ \
    --health-check-interval-seconds 30 \
    --health-check-timeout-seconds 5 \
    --healthy-threshold-count 2 \
    --unhealthy-threshold-count 3 \
    --matcher HttpCode=200

# 2. Create Application Load Balancer
aws elbv2 create-load-balancer \
    --name anihpj-alb \
    --subnets subnet-0abc123 subnet-0def456 subnet-0ghi789 \
    --security-groups sg-0alb123 \
    --scheme internet-facing \
    --type application \
    --ip-address-type ipv4 \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-alb Key=Environment,Value=production

# Output will include: LoadBalancerArn and DNSName
# DNSName: anihpj-alb-1234567890.us-east-1.elb.amazonaws.com

# 3. Create HTTP Listener (redirect to HTTPS)
aws elbv2 create-listener \
    --load-balancer-arn arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:loadbalancer/app/anihpj-alb/abc123 \
    --protocol HTTP \
    --port 80 \
    --default-actions Type=redirect,RedirectConfig='{Protocol=HTTPS,Port=443,StatusCode=HTTP_301}'

# 4. Create HTTPS Listener
aws elbv2 create-listener \
    --load-balancer-arn arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:loadbalancer/app/anihpj-alb/abc123 \
    --protocol HTTPS \
    --port 443 \
    --certificates CertificateArn=arn:aws:acm:us-east-1:123456789012:certificate/abc123 \
    --ssl-policy ELBSecurityPolicy-TLS-1-2-2017-01 \
    --default-actions Type=forward,TargetGroupArn=arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:targetgroup/anihpj-tg/abc123

# 5. Create path-based routing rules (advanced)
# Route /api/* to API servers
aws elbv2 create-rule \
    --listener-arn arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:listener/app/anihpj-alb/abc123/def456 \
    --priority 10 \
    --conditions Field=path-pattern,Values='/api/*' \
    --actions Type=forward,TargetGroupArn=arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:targetgroup/anihpj-api-tg/xyz789

# Route /static/* to static file servers or S3
aws elbv2 create-rule \
    --listener-arn arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:listener/app/anihpj-alb/abc123/def456 \
    --priority 20 \
    --conditions Field=path-pattern,Values='/static/*' \
    --actions Type=redirect,RedirectConfig='{Protocol=HTTPS,Host=static.anihpj.com,StatusCode=HTTP_301}'
🏥 Django Health Check Endpoint
# anihpj/jobpost/views.py
from django.http import JsonResponse
from django.db import connection
from django.core.cache import cache
import logging

logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

def health_check(request):
    """
    Health check endpoint for ALB
    Returns 200 if healthy, 503 if unhealthy
    """
    health_status = {
        'status': 'healthy',
        'checks': {}
    }
    is_healthy = True
    
    # Check database connectivity
    try:
        with connection.cursor() as cursor:
            cursor.execute("SELECT 1")
            health_status['checks']['database'] = 'ok'
    except Exception as e:
        health_status['checks']['database'] = f'error: {str(e)}'
        is_healthy = False
        logger.error(f"Database health check failed: {e}")
    
    # Check cache connectivity
    try:
        cache.set('health_check', 'ok', 10)
        if cache.get('health_check') == 'ok':
            health_status['checks']['cache'] = 'ok'
        else:
            health_status['checks']['cache'] = 'error'
            is_healthy = False
    except Exception as e:
        health_status['checks']['cache'] = f'error: {str(e)}'
        is_healthy = False
        logger.error(f"Cache health check failed: {e}")
    
    # Check disk space
    import shutil
    try:
        stat = shutil.disk_usage('/')
        free_percent = (stat.free / stat.total) * 100
        if free_percent < 10:
            health_status['checks']['disk'] = f'warning: {free_percent:.1f}% free'
            is_healthy = False
        else:
            health_status['checks']['disk'] = f'ok: {free_percent:.1f}% free'
    except Exception as e:
        health_status['checks']['disk'] = f'error: {str(e)}'
        is_healthy = False
    
    if is_healthy:
        return JsonResponse(health_status, status=200)
    else:
        health_status['status'] = 'unhealthy'
        return JsonResponse(health_status, status=503)

# anihpj/urls.py
from django.urls import path
from jobpost.views import health_check

urlpatterns = [
    # ... other patterns ...
    path('health/', health_check, name='health_check'),
]

💡 HA Best Practices for anihpj:
  • Deploy across at least 2 Availability Zones
  • Use Multi-AZ RDS for database
  • Store session data in ElastiCache, not local disk
  • Use S3 for static files and user uploads
  • Implement health checks on all services
  • Set up automated backups and disaster recovery

🎓 Advanced Topics

🚀 EC2 Fleet

Launch and manage thousands of EC2 instances with a single request. Mix On-Demand, Reserved, and Spot instances.

# Create EC2 Fleet for anihpj batch processing
aws ec2 create-fleet \
    --launch-template-configs '[
        {
            "LaunchTemplateSpecification": {
                "LaunchTemplateId": "lt-0abc123",
                "Version": "$Latest"
            },
            "Overrides": [
                {"InstanceType": "m5.large", "SubnetId": "subnet-0abc123"},
                {"InstanceType": "m5.xlarge", "SubnetId": "subnet-0def456"}
            ]
        }
    ]' \
    --target-capacity-specification '{
        "TotalTargetCapacity": 10,
        "OnDemandTargetCapacity": 2,
        "SpotTargetCapacity": 8,
        "DefaultTargetCapacityType": "spot"
    }' \
    --spot-options '{
        "AllocationStrategy": "diversified",
        "InstanceInterruptionBehavior": "terminate"
    }'
⚡ Enhanced Networking & Placement
🔌 Elastic Fabric Adapter (EFA) for HPC
EFA provides lower latency and higher throughput than TCP transport
for inter-instance communication.

Use cases:
• Machine learning training (distributed)
• Computational fluid dynamics
• Weather modeling
• Financial simulations

Not needed for typical Django web applications like anihpj.

sudo yum update -y
sudo yum install -y docker
sudo service docker start
sudo usermod -a -G docker ec2-user

# Build and run anihpj container
docker build -t anihpj:latest .
docker run -d -p 80:8000 \
    -e DATABASE_URL=postgresql://... \
    -e SECRET_KEY=... \
    --name anihpj-container \
    anihpj:latest

# More managed, integrates with ALB, Auto Scaling

# For complex microservices architectures
# Overkill for single Django application
💤 EC2 Hibernation
Hibernation saves RAM to EBS, faster boot than cold start.

┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  Standard Stop/Start:                              │
│  Stop → 30-60 seconds → Start                      │
│  • OS boots from scratch                           │
│  • Applications restart                            │
│  • Cache rebuilds                                  │
│                                                     │
│  With Hibernation:                                 │
│  Hibernate → 5-10 seconds → Resume                 │
│  • RAM restored from EBS                           │
│  • Applications resume instantly                   │
│  • Cache preserved                                 │
│                                                     │
│  Use for anihpj:                                   │
│  • Dev/staging environments (save costs)           │
│  • Preserve application state                      │
│  • Faster startup for scheduled workloads          │
└────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

# Enable hibernation
aws ec2 run-instances \
    --image-id ami-0c7217cdde317cfec \
    --instance-type m5.large \
    --hibernation-options Configured=true \
    --block-device-mappings '[
        {
            "DeviceName": "/dev/xvda",
            "Ebs": {
                "VolumeSize": 30,
                "Encrypted": true
            }
        }
    ]'
⚙️ Nitro System
AWS Nitro System is the underlying platform for modern EC2 instances.

Benefits:
✅ Better performance (dedicated hardware for networking, storage)
✅ Enhanced security (hypervisor offloaded to dedicated hardware)
✅ More instance sizes and types
✅ Bare metal instances available
✅ Better price/performance

All modern instance types (M5, C5, R5, T3, etc.) use Nitro System.

For anihpj: Always choose Nitro-based instances (t3, m5, c5, etc.)
over previous generation (t2, m4, c4).

🔒 Security Checklist
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│           SECURITY BEST PRACTICES CHECKLIST                      │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

│  ☐ Rotate IAM credentials regularly                             │
│  ☐ Use AWS Systems Manager Session Manager instead of SSH       │

│  ☐ Restrict inbound traffic to necessary ports only             │
│  ☐ Use VPC with private subnets for databases                   │
│  ☐ Enable VPC Flow Logs for traffic analysis                    │
│  ☐ Use AWS WAF for web application firewall                     │
│  ☐ Enable DDoS protection with Shield Standard/Advanced         │
│                                                                  │
│  DATA PROTECTION                                                 │
│  ☐ Enable EBS encryption for all volumes                        │
│  ☐ Enable encryption at rest for RDS databases                  │
│  ☐ Use SSL/TLS for data in transit                              │
│  ☐ Enable S3 bucket encryption                                  │
│  ☐ Use AWS KMS for key management                               │
│  ☐ Enable CloudTrail for audit logging                          │
│                                                                  │
│  PATCHING & UPDATES                                              │
│  ☐ Enable automatic security updates                            │
│  ☐ Use AWS Systems Manager Patch Manager                        │
│  ☐ Keep Django and dependencies updated                         │
│  ☐ Regularly scan for vulnerabilities                           │
│  ☐ Use immutable infrastructure (replace, not patch)            │
│                                                                  │
│  MONITORING & INCIDENT RESPONSE                                  │

│  ☐ Enable GuardDuty for threat detection                        │

│  ☐ Implement automated incident response                        │
│  ☐ Regular security audits and penetration testing              │
│                                                                  │
│  BACKUP & DISASTER RECOVERY                                      │
│  ☐ Enable automated EBS snapshots                               │
│  ☐ Enable RDS automated backups                                 │

│  ☐ Use cross-region replication for critical data               │
│                                                                  │

⚡ Performance Optimization
🎯 Django Performance on EC2
# 1. Use connection pooling for database
# settings.py
DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': 'anihpj',
        'USER': 'anihpj_user',
        'PASSWORD': os.environ['DB_PASSWORD'],
        'HOST': 'anihpj-db.abc123.us-east-1.rds.amazonaws.com',
        'PORT': '5432',
        'CONN_MAX_AGE': 600,  # Connection pooling
        'OPTIONS': {
            'connect_timeout': 10,
            'keepalives': 1,
            'keepalives_idle': 30,
        }
    }
}

# 2. Implement caching with ElastiCache
CACHES = {
    'default': {
        'BACKEND': 'django_redis.cache.RedisCache',
        'LOCATION': 'redis://anihpj-redis.abc123.cache.amazonaws.com:6379/1',
        'OPTIONS': {
            'CLIENT_CLASS': 'django_redis.client.DefaultClient',
            'CONNECTION_POOL_KWARGS': {
                'max_connections': 50,
                'retry_on_timeout': True
            },
            'SOCKET_CONNECT_TIMEOUT': 5,
            'SOCKET_TIMEOUT': 5,
        }
    }
}

# Cache expensive queries
from django.core.cache import cache
from jobpost.models import JobPost

def get_featured_jobs():
    cache_key = 'featured_jobs'
    jobs = cache.get(cache_key)
    if not jobs:
        jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(
            is_featured=True
        ).select_related('author', 'location').prefetch_related('skills')[:10]
        cache.set(cache_key, jobs, 3600)  # Cache for 1 hour
    return jobs

# 3. Use database query optimization
# Bad - N+1 queries
jobs = JobPost.objects.all()
for job in jobs:
    print(job.author.name)  # Additional query per job!

# Good - Single query with JOIN
jobs = JobPost.objects.select_related('author', 'location').all()
for job in jobs:
    print(job.author.name)  # No additional query

├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                  │
│  Step 1: Collect Metrics (2-4 weeks)                            │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
