🔧 Core Concepts & Terminology

💾 EBS Volumes

An EBS volume is a durable, block-level storage device that you attach to an EC2 instance. Once attached, you can create a file system, run a database, or use it like any raw block device.

💡 Key Characteristics:
  • Persistent: Data persists even if EC2 instance is stopped or terminated
  • AZ-specific: Volume must be in same Availability Zone as EC2 instance
  • Attachable/Detachable: Can be attached/detached from instances
  • Single-attach (default): Most volumes attach to one EC2 at a time
  • Multi-attach (io2): io2 volumes support up to 16 EC2 instances
📊 EBS Volume Types
Volume Type Description Performance Cost anihpj Use Case
gp3
(General Purpose SSD)		 Latest generation, best price/performance 3,000-16,000 IOPS
125-1,000 MiB/s		 $0.08/GB/month ✅ Recommended
DB + app storage
gp2
(General Purpose SSD)		 Previous generation 3-16,000 IOPS
128-250 MiB/s		 $0.10/GB/month ⚠️ Use gp3 instead
io2
(Provisioned IOPS SSD)		 High-performance, mission-critical Up to 64,000 IOPS
1,000 MiB/s
99.999% durability		 $0.125/GB/month
+ $0.065/IOPS		 🎯 High-traffic production
Critical databases
st1
(Throughput Optimized HDD)		 Low-cost HDD for frequent access Max 500 IOPS
500 MiB/s		 $0.045/GB/month 💾 Log archives
Data warehousing
sc1
(Cold HDD)		 Lowest cost for infrequent access Max 250 IOPS
250 MiB/s		 $0.015/GB/month ❄️ Cold backups
Archive storage

✅ anihpj Recommendation:

Use gp3 for all primary volumes (root, database, logs). It offers 20% cost savings over gp2 and baseline 3,000 IOPS is perfect for most Django applications. Upgrade to io2 only if you experience database performance bottlenecks.

📸 EBS Snapshots

Snapshots are point-in-time backups of EBS volumes stored in Amazon S3. They are incremental—only blocks that have changed since the last snapshot are saved.

📸 Snapshot Example for anihpj Database
# Create a snapshot of the database volume
aws ec2 create-snapshot \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123def456 \
    --description "anihpj-db-backup-2025-11-03" \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=snapshot,Tags=[{Key=Environment,Value=Production},{Key=Application,Value=anihpj},{Key=BackupType,Value=Daily}]'

# Output
{
    "SnapshotId": "snap-0def789ghi123",
    "VolumeId": "vol-0abc123def456",
    "State": "pending",
    "StartTime": "2025-11-03T10:00:00.000Z",
    "Progress": "0%",
    "Description": "anihpj-db-backup-2025-11-03"
}

# List all snapshots for anihpj
aws ec2 describe-snapshots \
    --owner-ids self \
    --filters "Name=tag:Application,Values=anihpj" \
    --query 'Snapshots[*].[SnapshotId,StartTime,VolumeSize,Description]' \
    --output table
🔒 EBS Encryption

EBS encryption uses AWS Key Management Service (KMS) to encrypt volumes at rest and during data transfer between the volume and instance.

  • Encrypted volumes: All data at rest, disk I/O, and snapshots are encrypted
  • Transparent: No performance impact, encryption/decryption handled automatically
  • KMS integration: Use AWS-managed keys or customer-managed keys (CMK)
  • Snapshot encryption: Snapshots inherit encryption from source volume
🔒 Create Encrypted Volume for anihpj Database
# Create encrypted EBS volume
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 100 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --iops 3000 \
    --throughput 125 \
    --encrypted \
    --kms-key-id arn:aws:kms:us-east-1:123456789012:key/abcd1234-a123-456a-a12b-a123b4cd56ef \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-db-encrypted},{Key=Environment,Value=Production},{Key=Encrypted,Value=true}]'
🛡️ Availability Zones

EBS volumes are automatically replicated within their Availability Zone to protect from component failure. However, they are AZ-specific:

⚠️ Important: EBS volumes can only attach to EC2 instances in the same AZ. For cross-AZ availability, create snapshots and restore in another AZ. For the anihpj job portal, place EC2 instance and EBS volume in same AZ (e.g., us-east-1a). Use multiple EBS volumes across AZs for high availability.

🚀 Getting Started with Amazon EBS

💾 Step 1: Create an EBS Volume
💾 Create gp3 Volume for anihpj Database
# Create 100GB gp3 volume for PostgreSQL database
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 100 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --iops 3000 \
    --throughput 125 \
    --encrypted \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-database-volume},{Key=Environment,Value=Production},{Key=Purpose,Value=PostgreSQL}]'

# Output
{
    "VolumeId": "vol-0abc123def456",
    "Size": 100,
    "VolumeType": "gp3",
    "Iops": 3000,
    "Throughput": 125,
    "State": "creating",
    "AvailabilityZone": "us-east-1a",
    "Encrypted": true
}
🔗 Step 2: Attach Volume to EC2 Instance
🔗 Attach EBS Volume to anihpj EC2 Instance
# Get EC2 instance ID
INSTANCE_ID=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
    --filters "Name=tag:Name,Values=anihpj-web-server" \
    --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].InstanceId' \
    --output text)

# Attach volume to instance (will appear as /dev/xvdf)
aws ec2 attach-volume \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123def456 \
    --instance-id $INSTANCE_ID \
    --device /dev/xvdf

# Verify attachment
aws ec2 describe-volumes \
    --volume-ids vol-0abc123def456 \
    --query 'Volumes[0].Attachments[0].[State,Device,InstanceId]' \
    --output table
⚙️ Step 3: Format and Mount the Volume
⚙️ Format, Mount, and Configure EBS Volume
# SSH into EC2 instance
ssh -i anihpj-keypair.pem ubuntu@ec2-instance-ip

# Check available disks
lsblk

# Output:
# NAME    MAJ:MIN RM  SIZE RO TYPE MOUNTPOINT
# xvda    202:0    0   30G  0 disk 
# └─xvda1 202:1    0   30G  0 part /
# xvdf    202:80   0  100G  0 disk    ← New EBS volume

# Check if filesystem exists (new volumes won't have one)
sudo file -s /dev/xvdf
# Output: /dev/xvdf: data  (no filesystem)

# Create ext4 filesystem
sudo mkfs -t ext4 /dev/xvdf

# Create mount point for PostgreSQL
sudo mkdir -p /var/lib/postgresql/data

# Mount the volume
sudo mount /dev/xvdf /var/lib/postgresql/data

# Verify mount
df -h | grep xvdf
# /dev/xvdf       100G   61M   95G   1% /var/lib/postgresql/data

# Set proper ownership for PostgreSQL
sudo chown -R postgres:postgres /var/lib/postgresql/data
sudo chmod 700 /var/lib/postgresql/data
🐍 Step 4: Configure Django to Use EBS Volume
🐍 anihpj Django Database Configuration
# anihpj/settings.py

import os
from pathlib import Path

# Database on EBS volume
DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': 'anihpj_db',
        'USER': 'anihpj_user',
        'PASSWORD': os.environ.get('DB_PASSWORD'),
        'HOST': 'localhost',  # PostgreSQL on same EC2 instance
        'PORT': '5432',
        'OPTIONS': {
            'connect_timeout': 10,
        },
        'CONN_MAX_AGE': 600,  # Connection pooling
    }
}

# Ensure PostgreSQL data directory is on EBS volume
# In postgresql.conf:
# data_directory = '/var/lib/postgresql/data'

# Application logs on EBS volume
LOGGING = {
    'version': 1,
    'disable_existing_loggers': False,
    'handlers': {
        'file': {
            'level': 'INFO',
            'class': 'logging.FileHandler',
            'filename': '/var/log/anihpj/application.log',  # On EBS log volume
            'formatter': 'verbose',
        },
        'error_file': {
            'level': 'ERROR',
            'class': 'logging.FileHandler',
            'filename': '/var/log/anihpj/errors.log',
            'formatter': 'verbose',
        },
    },
    'formatters': {
        'verbose': {
            'format': '{levelname} {asctime} {module} {message}',
            'style': '{',
        },
    },
    'loggers': {
        'django': {
            'handlers': ['file', 'error_file'],
            'level': 'INFO',
            'propagate': True,
        },
        'anihpj': {
            'handlers': ['file', 'error_file'],
            'level': 'DEBUG',
            'propagate': False,
        },
    },
}
📝 Step 5: Auto-Mount on Reboot (fstab)

To ensure the EBS volume automatically mounts after EC2 instance reboots, add it to /etc/fstab.

📝 Configure Auto-Mount in /etc/fstab
# Get the UUID of the volume (more reliable than device name)
sudo blkid /dev/xvdf
# /dev/xvdf: UUID="aebf131c-6957-451e-8d34-ec978d9581ae" TYPE="ext4"

# Backup fstab
sudo cp /etc/fstab /etc/fstab.backup

# Add entry to fstab (use UUID for reliability)
echo 'UUID=aebf131c-6957-451e-8d34-ec978d9581ae  /var/lib/postgresql/data  ext4  defaults,nofail  0  2' | sudo tee -a /etc/fstab

# Test the configuration (should mount without errors)
sudo umount /var/lib/postgresql/data
sudo mount -a

# Verify mount
df -h | grep postgresql
# /dev/xvdf       100G   61M   95G   1% /var/lib/postgresql/data

# Note: 'nofail' option allows system to boot even if volume fails to mount
💡 Best Practice: Always use UUID instead of device names (like /dev/xvdf) in fstab, as device names can change across reboots.

🔑 Key Features & Capabilities

💾 Backup with Snapshots

EBS snapshots provide incremental backups of volumes to S3, enabling disaster recovery and cross-AZ/region replication.

💾 Automated Daily Backup Script for anihpj Database
# backup_ebs_volume.py
import boto3
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
import os

ec2 = boto3.client('ec2', region_name='us-east-1')

def create_snapshot(volume_id, description, retention_days=7):
    """Create EBS snapshot with automatic cleanup"""
    
    # Create snapshot
    response = ec2.create_snapshot(
        VolumeId=volume_id,
        Description=f"{description} - {datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M')}",
        TagSpecifications=[
            {
                'ResourceType': 'snapshot',
                'Tags': [
                    {'Key': 'Application', 'Value': 'anihpj'},
                    {'Key': 'BackupType', 'Value': 'Daily'},
                    {'Key': 'RetentionDays', 'Value': str(retention_days)},
                    {'Key': 'CreatedBy', 'Value': 'AutomatedBackup'},
                    {'Key': 'Timestamp', 'Value': datetime.now().isoformat()}
                ]
            }
        ]
    )
    
    snapshot_id = response['SnapshotId']
    print(f"✅ Created snapshot: {snapshot_id}")
    
    # Delete old snapshots (older than retention period)
    delete_old_snapshots(volume_id, retention_days)
    
    return snapshot_id

def delete_old_snapshots(volume_id, retention_days):
    """Delete snapshots older than retention period"""
    
    cutoff_date = datetime.now() - timedelta(days=retention_days)
    
    # Get all snapshots for this volume
    snapshots = ec2.describe_snapshots(
        Filters=[
            {'Name': 'volume-id', 'Values': [volume_id]},
            {'Name': 'tag:Application', 'Values': ['anihpj']},
            {'Name': 'tag:BackupType', 'Values': ['Daily']}
        ],
        OwnerIds=['self']
    )['Snapshots']
    
    for snapshot in snapshots:
        snapshot_date = snapshot['StartTime'].replace(tzinfo=None)
        if snapshot_date < cutoff_date:
            try:
                ec2.delete_snapshot(SnapshotId=snapshot['SnapshotId'])
                print(f"🗑️  Deleted old snapshot: {snapshot['SnapshotId']} from {snapshot_date}")
            except Exception as e:
                print(f"❌ Failed to delete {snapshot['SnapshotId']}: {e}")

# Usage for anihpj database volume
if __name__ == '__main__':
    DB_VOLUME_ID = 'vol-0abc123def456'  # anihpj database volume
    create_snapshot(
        volume_id=DB_VOLUME_ID,
        description='anihpj PostgreSQL database backup',
        retention_days=7  # Keep 7 days of backups
    )
🔄 Restore Volume from Snapshot
# List available snapshots
aws ec2 describe-snapshots \
    --owner-ids self \
    --filters "Name=tag:Application,Values=anihpj" \
    --query 'Snapshots | sort_by(@, &StartTime) | [-5:].[SnapshotId,StartTime,VolumeSize,Description]' \
    --output table

# Create new volume from snapshot
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --snapshot-id snap-0def789ghi123 \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --iops 3000 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-db-restored},{Key=RestoreDate,Value=2025-11-03}]'

# Attach to EC2 instance
aws ec2 attach-volume \
    --volume-id vol-NEW123456 \
    --instance-id i-anihpj-instance \
    --device /dev/xvdg
📏 Resize Volumes (Expand Storage)

EBS volumes can be resized without downtime. You can increase volume size, change volume type, or adjust IOPS/throughput.

📏 Expand anihpj Database Volume from 100GB to 200GB
# Step 1: Modify volume size (no downtime required)
aws ec2 modify-volume \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123def456 \
    --size 200 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --iops 5000 \
    --throughput 200

# Step 2: Monitor modification progress
aws ec2 describe-volumes-modifications \
    --volume-ids vol-0abc123def456 \
    --query 'VolumesModifications[0].[ModificationState,Progress]' \
    --output table

# Step 3: Extend filesystem (on EC2 instance)
# SSH into instance
ssh -i anihpj-keypair.pem ubuntu@instance-ip

# Check current filesystem size
df -h /var/lib/postgresql/data
# Filesystem      Size  Used Avail Use% Mounted on
# /dev/xvdf       100G   85G   15G  85% /var/lib/postgresql/data

# Extend ext4 filesystem to use new space
sudo resize2fs /dev/xvdf

# Verify new size
df -h /var/lib/postgresql/data
# Filesystem      Size  Used Avail Use% Mounted on
# /dev/xvdf       200G   85G  115G  43% /var/lib/postgresql/data
⚠️ Important Notes: Volume size can only be increased, not decreased. Wait at least 6 hours between modifications. Performance changes take effect within 24 hours (but size is immediate). Always create a snapshot before major modifications.
🚚 Volume Migration (Change AZ or Type)
🚚 Migrate anihpj Volume to Different AZ
# Scenario: Move database from us-east-1a to us-east-1b

# Step 1: Create snapshot
aws ec2 create-snapshot \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123def456 \
    --description "anihpj-db-migration-snapshot"

# Step 2: Create new volume in target AZ from snapshot
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --snapshot-id snap-0migration789 \
    --availability-zone us-east-1b \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --iops 5000 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-db-us-east-1b}]'

# Step 3: Stop application, detach old volume, attach new volume
# (Requires application downtime)
🔗 Multi-Attach (io2 Volumes Only)

io2 Block Express volumes support Multi-Attach, allowing a single volume to be attached to up to 16 EC2 instances simultaneously in the same AZ.

📌 Use Case for anihpj:

Multi-Attach is useful for clustered applications requiring shared storage. For anihpj, this could be used for:

  • PostgreSQL clusters (with proper clustering software like Patroni)
  • Shared application cache between multiple web servers
  • Note: Most Django applications don't need Multi-Attach; use EFS for shared file storage instead
⚡ Fast Snapshot Restore (FSR)

FSR eliminates the I/O performance penalty when creating volumes from snapshots. Volumes created with FSR are immediately initialized with full performance.

⚡ Enable Fast Snapshot Restore
# Enable FSR for snapshot in specific AZ
aws ec2 enable-fast-snapshot-restores \
    --availability-zones us-east-1a us-east-1b \
    --source-snapshot-ids snap-0def789ghi123

# Cost: $0.75 per snapshot per AZ per month (only enable when needed)

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

💵 EBS Pricing Model

EBS charges based on:

  • Provisioned Storage: GB/month for allocated space (pay for provisioned, not used)
  • Provisioned IOPS: For io2 volumes, additional charge per IOPS
  • Snapshots: GB/month for incremental snapshot storage in S3
  • Fast Snapshot Restore: Per snapshot per AZ per month
📊 Cost Breakdown for anihpj
Resource Volume Type Size IOPS Monthly Cost
Root Volume
(OS + Application)		 gp3 30 GB 3,000 (baseline) 30 × $0.08 = $2.40
Database Volume
(PostgreSQL data)		 gp3 100 GB 3,000 (baseline) 100 × $0.08 = $8.00
Log Volume
(Application logs)		 gp3 50 GB 3,000 (baseline) 50 × $0.08 = $4.00
Snapshots
(7-day retention)		 - ~40 GB
(incremental)		 - 40 × $0.05 = $2.00
Total EBS Cost $16.40/month
💡 Cost Comparison (100GB Database Volume): gp3: $8.00/month (✅ Recommended), gp2: $10.00/month (25% more expensive), io2: $207.50/month for 3,000 IOPS, st1 (HDD): $4.50/month (but much slower for databases). Result: gp3 offers best price/performance for anihpj database workloads.
💡 Cost Optimization Tips
  1. Use gp3 instead of gp2:
    • 20% cost savings for same performance
    • Baseline 3,000 IOPS sufficient for most Django apps
    • Can scale IOPS independently from storage
  2. Right-size your volumes:
    📊 Monitor Volume Usage
    # Check disk usage on EC2 instance
df -h

# CloudWatch metric for volume usage
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EBS \
    --metric-name VolumeReadOps \
    --dimensions Name=VolumeId,Value=vol-0abc123def456 \
    --start-time 2025-10-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2025-11-01T00:00:00Z \
    --period 86400 \
    --statistics Average
  3. Delete unused snapshots:
    🗑️ Cleanup Old Snapshots
    # Find snapshots older than 30 days
aws ec2 describe-snapshots \
    --owner-ids self \
    --filters "Name=tag:Application,Values=anihpj" \
    --query "Snapshots[?StartTime<='$(date -d '30 days ago' -Iseconds)'].[SnapshotId,StartTime,VolumeSize]" \
    --output table

# Delete specific snapshot
aws ec2 delete-snapshot --snapshot-id snap-old123456
  4. Use st1 (HDD) for infrequently accessed data:
    • Log archives: st1 ($0.045/GB) vs gp3 ($0.08/GB) = 44% savings
    • Cold backups: sc1 ($0.015/GB) = 81% savings
  5. Leverage snapshot lifecycle policies:
    • Automate snapshot creation and deletion
    • Reduce manual management overhead
    • Ensure compliance without over-retention
  6. Delete detached volumes:
    🔍 Find Detached Volumes
    # List all detached (available) volumes
aws ec2 describe-volumes \
    --filters "Name=status,Values=available" \
    --query 'Volumes[*].[VolumeId,Size,VolumeType,CreateTime,Tags[?Key==`Name`].Value|[0]]' \
    --output table

# Delete unused volume (after confirming no data needed)
aws ec2 delete-volume --volume-id vol-unused123

💰 anihpj Cost Optimization Strategy:

  • Development: gp3 30GB ($2.40/mo) - sufficient for testing
  • Production: gp3 100GB ($8/mo) + daily snapshots ($2/mo) = $10/month
  • High-Traffic Production: io2 100GB + 10,000 IOPS = $262/month (only if needed)

Recommendation: Start with gp3, monitor performance, upgrade to io2 only if experiencing bottlenecks.

📈 Scalability & High Availability

⚡ Performance Scaling

EBS volumes can scale performance by:

  1. Increasing Volume Size (gp3/gp2):
    • gp2: 3 IOPS per GB (e.g., 334GB = 1,000 IOPS, 5,334GB = 16,000 IOPS)
    • gp3: Baseline 3,000 IOPS regardless of size
    • gp3: Pay separately to scale IOPS (3,000 - 16,000) and throughput (125 - 1,000 MiB/s)
  2. Provisioned IOPS (io2):
    • Up to 64,000 IOPS per volume
    • Up to 1,000 MiB/s throughput
    • 99.999% durability (vs 99.8-99.9% for gp3)
    • Best for mission-critical production databases
  3. EBS-Optimized Instances:
    • Dedicated bandwidth for EBS traffic
    • Prevents network congestion affecting disk I/O
    • Most modern instance types are EBS-optimized by default
⚡ Scale anihpj Database Performance
# Current: gp3 100GB with baseline 3,000 IOPS, 125 MiB/s
# Target: 10,000 IOPS, 500 MiB/s for high-traffic periods

# Modify volume to increase performance
aws ec2 modify-volume \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123def456 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --iops 10000 \
    --throughput 500

# Cost impact:
# - Storage: 100GB × $0.08 = $8.00/month (unchanged)
# - Additional IOPS: (10,000 - 3,000) × $0.005 = $35.00/month
# - Additional throughput: (500 - 125) / 125 × $0.04 per MiB/s = $12.00/month
# Total: $55/month (vs $207/month for io2 with 10,000 IOPS)
💪 RAID Configurations for Enhanced Performance

For workloads requiring higher IOPS or throughput than a single volume can provide, use RAID:

  • RAID 0 (Striping): Combines multiple volumes for higher performance
    • 2× 100GB gp3 = 6,000 IOPS, 250 MiB/s throughput
    • ❌ No redundancy - if one volume fails, all data is lost
    • ✅ Use for temporary data or when using RDS/Aurora instead
  • RAID 1 (Mirroring): Redundancy for increased durability
    • Not recommended for EBS (AWS already provides 99.999% durability)
    • Use snapshots and Multi-AZ deployments instead
  • RAID 10 (Striping + Mirroring): Both performance and redundancy
    • Requires 4+ volumes (expensive)
    • Better to use io2 with Multi-AZ RDS for databases
⚠️ RAID Best Practices
  • For anihpj: RAID is generally NOT recommended
  • Single gp3 volume with 3,000-16,000 IOPS is sufficient for most Django apps
  • If you need higher performance, use RDS instead of self-managed PostgreSQL
  • RAID increases complexity and cost without significant benefit for small-medium workloads

🎯 anihpj Scalability Strategy:

  1. Start Simple: Single gp3 100GB volume with baseline 3,000 IOPS
  2. Monitor Performance: Use CloudWatch to track IOPS, throughput, latency
  3. Scale Vertically: Increase volume IOPS/throughput as needed (up to 16,000 IOPS)
  4. Consider Managed Services: If scaling beyond 16,000 IOPS, migrate to Amazon RDS Aurora
  5. Multi-AZ for HA: Use RDS Multi-AZ or manual snapshot-based recovery for disaster recovery

🎯 Advanced Topics

7.1 Provisioned IOPS SSD (io2/io2 Block Express)

For workloads requiring consistent, low-latency performance:

# Create io2 volume with 10,000 IOPS for high-performance anihpj database
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 100 \
    --volume-type io2 \
    --iops 10000 \
    --encrypted \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-db-io2},{Key=Environment,Value=production}]'

# For extreme performance: io2 Block Express (up to 256,000 IOPS)
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 500 \
    --volume-type io2 \
    --iops 64000 \
    --throughput 4000 \
    --encrypted

7.2 CloudWatch Monitoring Setup

Comprehensive monitoring for anihpj EBS volumes:

# Python script: monitor_ebs_metrics.py
import boto3
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name='us-east-1')

def get_ebs_metrics(volume_id, metric_name, hours=24):
    """Get EBS CloudWatch metrics for anihpj volumes"""
    end_time = datetime.utcnow()
    start_time = end_time - timedelta(hours=hours)
    
    response = cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics(
        Namespace='AWS/EBS',
        MetricName=metric_name,
        Dimensions=[{'Name': 'VolumeId', 'Value': volume_id}],
        StartTime=start_time,
        EndTime=end_time,
        Period=3600,  # 1-hour intervals
        Statistics=['Average', 'Maximum']
    )
    
    return response['Datapoints']

# Monitor key metrics for anihpj database volume
volume_id = 'vol-0123456789abcdef0'  # anihpj database volume

# Critical metrics to track
metrics = {
    'VolumeReadOps': 'Read Operations per second',
    'VolumeWriteOps': 'Write Operations per second', 
    'VolumeQueueLength': 'Queue depth (target: <10)',
    'VolumeTotalReadTime': 'Read latency',
    'VolumeTotalWriteTime': 'Write latency'
}

for metric_name, description in metrics.items():
    data = get_ebs_metrics(volume_id, metric_name)
    if data:
        avg_value = sum(d['Average'] for d in data) / len(data)
        max_value = max(d['Maximum'] for d in data)
        print(f"{description}: Avg={avg_value:.2f}, Max={max_value:.2f}")

7.3 Data Lifecycle Manager (DLM) Automation

Automate snapshot creation and retention for anihpj:

# Create comprehensive DLM lifecycle policy
aws dlm create-lifecycle-policy \
    --execution-role-arn arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/AWSDataLifecycleManagerDefaultRole \
    --description "Automated snapshots for anihpj EBS volumes with tiered retention" \
    --state ENABLED \
    --policy-details '{
        "ResourceTypes": ["VOLUME"],
        "TargetTags": [
            {"Key": "Project", "Value": "anihpj"},
            {"Key": "Backup", "Value": "true"}
        ],
        "Schedules": [
            {
                "Name": "DailySnapshots",
                "CreateRule": {
                    "Interval": 24,
                    "IntervalUnit": "HOURS", 
                    "Times": ["03:00"],
                    "CronExpression": "cron(0 3 * * ? *)"
                },
                "RetainRule": {
                    "Count": 7,
                    "Interval": 1,
                    "IntervalUnit": "DAYS"
                },
                "TagsToAdd": [
                    {"Key": "SnapshotType", "Value": "daily"},
                    {"Key": "Project", "Value": "anihpj"}
                ],
                "CopyTags": true,
                "VariableTags": [
                    {"Key": "instance-id", "Value": "$(instance-id)"}
                ]
            },
            {
                "Name": "WeeklySnapshots", 
                "CreateRule": {
                    "CronExpression": "cron(0 5 ? * SUN *)"
                },
                "RetainRule": {
                    "Count": 4
                },
                "TagsToAdd": [
                    {"Key": "SnapshotType", "Value": "weekly"}
                ]
            }
        ]
    }'

7.4 EBS Encryption with KMS

Advanced encryption setup for anihpj data protection:

# Create custom KMS key for anihpj with proper key policy
aws kms create-key \
    --description "anihpj EBS encryption key with automatic rotation" \
    --key-usage ENCRYPT_DECRYPT \
    --key-spec SYMMETRIC_DEFAULT \
    --policy '{
        "Version": "2012-10-17",
        "Statement": [
            {
                "Sid": "Enable IAM User Permissions",
                "Effect": "Allow",
                "Principal": {"AWS": "arn:aws:iam::123456789012:root"},
                "Action": "kms:*",
                "Resource": "*"
            },
            {
                "Sid": "Allow EBS Service",
                "Effect": "Allow", 
                "Principal": {"Service": "ec2.amazonaws.com"},
                "Action": [
                    "kms:Decrypt",
                    "kms:GenerateDataKey",
                    "kms:CreateGrant"
                ],
                "Resource": "*",
                "Condition": {
                    "StringEquals": {
                        "kms:ViaService": "ec2.us-east-1.amazonaws.com"
                    }
                }
            }
        ]
    }' \
    --tags TagKey=Project,TagValue=anihpj TagKey=Purpose,TagValue=EBSEncryption

# Enable automatic key rotation (rotates annually)
aws kms enable-key-rotation --key-id alias/anihpj-ebs

# Create alias for easier management
aws kms create-alias \
    --alias-name alias/anihpj-ebs \
    --target-key-id $KEY_ID

# Enable encryption by default for all new volumes in account
aws ec2 enable-ebs-encryption-by-default --region us-east-1
aws ec2 put-ebs-default-kms-key-id --kms-key-id alias/anihpj-ebs --region us-east-1

✅ Best Practices

8.1 Security Best Practices

🔒 Security Checklist for anihpj EBS Volumes
  • Encrypt Everything: Enable encryption for all volumes storing sensitive data (user profiles, applications, resumes)
  • Use Custom KMS Keys: Better audit trail and access control than AWS managed keys
  • Implement IAM Policies: Restrict EBS operations with least privilege principle
  • Secure Snapshots: Never share unencrypted snapshots, use cross-region encrypted copies
  • Resource Tagging: Use consistent tags for governance (Project=anihpj, Environment=prod, Owner=team)
# IAM policy for anihpj EBS operations with least privilege
{
    "Version": "2012-10-17",
    "Statement": [
        {
            "Sid": "EBSVolumeOperations",
            "Effect": "Allow",
            "Action": [
                "ec2:CreateVolume",
                "ec2:AttachVolume", 
                "ec2:DetachVolume",
                "ec2:ModifyVolume",
                "ec2:DescribeVolumes",
                "ec2:DescribeVolumeStatus"
            ],
            "Resource": "*",
            "Condition": {
                "StringEquals": {
                    "aws:RequestedRegion": ["us-east-1", "us-west-2"],
                    "ec2:ResourceTag/Project": "anihpj"
                }
            }
        },
        {
            "Sid": "SnapshotOperations", 
            "Effect": "Allow",
            "Action": [
                "ec2:CreateSnapshot",
                "ec2:DeleteSnapshot", 
                "ec2:DescribeSnapshots",
                "ec2:CopySnapshot"
            ],
            "Resource": "*",
            "Condition": {
                "StringEquals": {
                    "ec2:ResourceTag/Project": "anihpj"
                }
            }
        },
        {
            "Sid": "KMSAccess",
            "Effect": "Allow", 
            "Action": [
                "kms:Decrypt",
                "kms:GenerateDataKey",
                "kms:CreateGrant",
                "kms:DescribeKey"
            ],
            "Resource": "arn:aws:kms:*:123456789012:key/*",
            "Condition": {
                "StringEquals": {
                    "kms:ViaService": ["ec2.us-east-1.amazonaws.com", "ec2.us-west-2.amazonaws.com"]
                }
            }
        }
    ]
}

8.2 Performance Best Practices

🚀 Performance Optimization for anihpj
  • Choose gp3 by Default: 20% cheaper than gp2 with independent IOPS/throughput scaling
  • Right-Size Initially: Start with 100GB for database, 50GB for logs, monitor and adjust
  • Use EBS-Optimized Instances: Dedicated bandwidth prevents network contention
  • Pre-Warm Restored Volumes: Read all blocks before production use to eliminate initialization penalty
  • Optimize Application I/O: Use connection pooling, batch writes, proper indexing
  • Monitor Queue Depth: Keep average queue length <10 for good performance
# Django settings optimization for EBS storage
# anihpj/settings.py

# Database connection optimization
DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': 'anihpj_db',
        'USER': 'anihpj_user',

        'PORT': '5432',
        'OPTIONS': {
            # Connection pooling for better EBS performance

            'connect_timeout': 10,

        },
        'CONN_MAX_AGE': 600,  # Keep connections open for 10 minutes
        'CONN_HEALTH_CHECKS': True,  # Check connection health

        'file': {

            'class': 'logging.handlers.RotatingFileHandler',

            'maxBytes': 50 * 1024 * 1024,  # 50MB per file
            'backupCount': 5,               # Keep 5 rotated files
            'formatter': 'verbose',
        },
        'error_file': {
            'level': 'ERROR',
            'class': 'logging.handlers.RotatingFileHandler',
            'filename': '/mnt/logs/anihpj_errors.log',

            'backupCount': 10,              # Keep 10 error files
            'formatter': 'verbose',
        },

    'loggers': {
        'django': {
            'handlers': ['file', 'error_file'],
            'level': 'INFO',
        },
        'anihpj': {  # Custom application logs
            'handlers': ['file'],
            'level': 'INFO', 
        },
    },

8.3 Cost Management Best Practices

# Python script: ebs_cost_optimizer.py
import boto3
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
import json

ec2 = boto3.client('ec2', region_name='us-east-1')
cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name='us-east-1') 

def analyze_ebs_costs():
    """Comprehensive cost analysis for anihpj EBS usage"""
    
    # Get all anihpj volumes
    volumes = ec2.describe_volumes(
        Filters=[{'Name': 'tag:Project', 'Values': ['anihpj']}]
    )
    
    total_cost = 0
    recommendations = []
    
    print("📊 anihpj EBS Cost Analysis")
    print("=" * 50)
    
    for volume in volumes['Volumes']:
        vol_id = volume['VolumeId']
        size = volume['Size']
        vol_type = volume['VolumeType'] 
        state = volume['State']
        
        # Get volume name from tags
        vol_name = next((tag['Value'] for tag in volume.get('Tags', []) 
                        if tag['Key'] == 'Name'), 'unnamed')
        
        # Calculate monthly cost
        cost_per_gb = {
            'gp3': 0.08, 'gp2': 0.10, 'io2': 0.125, 
            'st1': 0.045, 'sc1': 0.015
        }
        
        monthly_cost = size * cost_per_gb.get(vol_type, 0.08)
        
        # Add IOPS cost for gp3/io2
        if vol_type == 'gp3' and volume.get('Iops', 3000) > 3000:
            extra_iops = volume.get('Iops', 3000) - 3000
            monthly_cost += extra_iops * 0.005
            
        if vol_type == 'io2':
            monthly_cost += volume.get('Iops', 100) * 0.065
            
        total_cost += monthly_cost
        
        print(f"Volume: {vol_name} ({vol_id})")
        print(f"  Size: {size}GB, Type: {vol_type}, State: {state}")
        print(f"  Monthly Cost: ${monthly_cost:.2f}")
        
        # Generate recommendations
        if state == 'available':
            recommendations.append(f"⚠️  Unused volume {vol_name}: ${monthly_cost:.2f}/month waste")
            
        if vol_type == 'gp2':
            gp3_cost = size * 0.08
            savings = monthly_cost - gp3_cost
            recommendations.append(f"💡 Convert {vol_name} to gp3: Save ${savings:.2f}/month")
            
        # Check utilization (requires CloudWatch agent data)
        try:
            utilization = get_disk_utilization(vol_id)
            if utilization and utilization < 50:
                recommendations.append(f"📉 {vol_name} only {utilization:.0f}% used: Consider downsizing")
        except:
            pass
    
    print(f"\nTotal Monthly Cost: ${total_cost:.2f}")
    print("\n📋 Cost Optimization Recommendations:")
    for i, rec in enumerate(recommendations, 1):
        print(f"{i}. {rec}")
    
    return total_cost, recommendations

def find_old_snapshots(days=90):
    """Find and cost old snapshots for cleanup"""
    snapshots = ec2.describe_snapshots(
        OwnerIds=['self'],
        Filters=[{'Name': 'tag:Project', 'Values': ['anihpj']}]
    )
    
    cutoff_date = datetime.now().replace(tzinfo=None) - timedelta(days=days)
    old_snapshots = []
    total_size = 0
    
    for snap in snapshots['Snapshots']:
        start_time = snap['StartTime'].replace(tzinfo=None)
        if start_time < cutoff_date:
            size_gb = snap['VolumeSize']
            total_size += size_gb 
            cost = size_gb * 0.05  # $0.05 per GB per month
            old_snapshots.append({
                'id': snap['SnapshotId'],
                'size': size_gb,
                'cost': cost,
                'age_days': (datetime.now().replace(tzinfo=None) - start_time).days
            })
    
    if old_snapshots:
        print(f"\n📸 Found {len(old_snapshots)} old snapshots ({total_size}GB)")
        print(f"Potential savings: ${total_size * 0.05:.2f}/month")
        
        for snap in sorted(old_snapshots, key=lambda x: x['age_days'], reverse=True)[:5]:
            print(f"  - {snap['id']}: {snap['size']}GB, {snap['age_days']} days old, ${snap['cost']:.2f}/month")
    
    return old_snapshots

def get_disk_utilization(volume_id):
    """Get disk utilization from CloudWatch (requires CW agent)"""
    try:
        response = cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics(
            Namespace='CWAgent',
            MetricName='disk_used_percent',
            Dimensions=[{'Name': 'VolumeId', 'Value': volume_id}],
            StartTime=datetime.utcnow() - timedelta(hours=24),
            EndTime=datetime.utcnow(),
            Period=3600,
            Statistics=['Average']
        )
        
        if response['Datapoints']:
            return sum(d['Average'] for d in response['Datapoints']) / len(response['Datapoints'])
    except:
        pass
    return None

if __name__ == "__main__":
    analyze_ebs_costs()
    find_old_snapshots(days=90)

  • Log Volume: 50GB gp3 (Django/PostgreSQL logs) - $4/month
  • Snapshots: Daily with 7-day retention - ~$2/month
  • Total Storage Cost: $16.40/month
# Complete anihpj database setup on EBS
# Step 1: Create optimized PostgreSQL configuration
# /etc/postgresql/14/main/postgresql.conf

# Memory settings (for t3.medium: 4GB RAM)
shared_buffers = 1GB                    # 25% of RAM
effective_cache_size = 3GB              # 75% of RAM  
work_mem = 4MB                          # Per connection working memory
maintenance_work_mem = 256MB            # For VACUUM, CREATE INDEX

# Connection settings

# WAL settings for EBS
wal_level = replica
max_wal_size = 1GB
min_wal_size = 80MB
checkpoint_completion_target = 0.9      # Spread checkpoints
wal_buffers = 16MB                      # WAL buffer size

# Logging for troubleshooting

log_duration = on                       # Log query duration
log_min_duration_statement = 1000       # Log slow queries (>1 second)

# anihpj models for file uploads
# jobpost/models.py
from django.db import models
from django.core.validators import FileExtensionValidator

class Company(models.Model):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=200)
    logo = models.ImageField(
        upload_to='company_logos/%Y/%m/%d/',
        blank=True, null=True,
        validators=[FileExtensionValidator(['jpg', 'jpeg', 'png'])],
        help_text="Upload company logo (JPG, PNG - max 2MB)"
    )

class JobSeeker(models.Model):
    user = models.OneToOneField('auth.User', on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    profile_picture = models.ImageField(
        upload_to='profile_pictures/%Y/%m/%d/', 
        blank=True, null=True,
        validators=[FileExtensionValidator(['jpg', 'jpeg', 'png'])]
    )

class JobApplication(models.Model):
    applicant = models.ForeignKey('JobSeeker', on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    job = models.ForeignKey('JobPost', on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    resume = models.FileField(
        upload_to='resumes/%Y/%m/%d/',
        validators=[FileExtensionValidator(['pdf', 'doc', 'docx'])],
        help_text="Upload resume (PDF, DOC, DOCX - max 5MB)"
    )
    cover_letter = models.FileField(
        upload_to='cover_letters/%Y/%m/%d/',
        blank=True, null=True,
        validators=[FileExtensionValidator(['pdf', 'doc', 'docx'])]
    )

9.3 Log Management and Archival

Scenario: Tiered log storage for anihpj with cost optimization

# Multi-tier log storage strategy for anihpj

# Tier 1: Active logs (gp3 - fast access for recent data)
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 20 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-logs-active},{Key=Tier,Value=hot}]'

# Tier 2: Archive logs (st1 - cheaper for old data)  
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 200 \
    --volume-type st1 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-logs-archive},{Key=Tier,Value=cold}]'

# Mount both volumes
sudo mkdir -p /var/log/anihpj/{active,archive}
sudo mount /dev/xvdi /var/log/anihpj/active
sudo mount /dev/xvdj /var/log/anihpj/archive

# Automated log rotation and archival
# /etc/logrotate.d/anihpj
/var/log/anihpj/active/*.log {
    daily
    rotate 30                      # Keep 30 days in active storage
    compress
    delaycompress
    missingok
    notifempty
    create 0640 www-data adm
    sharedscripts
    
    postrotate
        # Move logs older than 30 days to archive storage
        find /var/log/anihpj/active -name "*.log.*.gz" -mtime +30 \
            -exec mv {} /var/log/anihpj/archive/ \;
        
        # Restart Django app to reopen log files
        systemctl reload nginx
        supervisorctl restart anihpj
    endscript
}

# Archive storage cleanup (keep 1 year)
/var/log/anihpj/archive/*.log.*.gz {
    weekly
    rotate 52                      # Keep 52 weeks (1 year)
    missingok
    notifempty
    
    postrotate
        # Remove logs older than 1 year
        find /var/log/anihpj/archive -name "*.log.*.gz" -mtime +365 -delete
    endscript
}

# Cost comparison for log storage:
# Hot storage (20GB gp3): $1.60/month
# Cold storage (200GB st1): $9.00/month  
# Total: $10.60/month vs $17.60 (all gp3) = 40% savings

    --volume-type gp3 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-db-dev},{Key=Environment,Value=development}]'

# 3. Data sanitization script for development environment
# sanitize_dev_data.py
import os
import django
os.environ.setdefault('DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE', 'anihpj.settings.development')
django.setup()

from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import JobSeeker, JobApplication
from faker import Faker

fake = Faker()

def sanitize_development_data():
    """Replace sensitive data with fake data for development"""
    
    # Anonymize user data
    for user in User.objects.all():
        if not user.is_superuser:
            user.first_name = fake.first_name()
            user.last_name = fake.last_name()
            user.email = fake.email()
            user.save()
    
    # Anonymize job seeker profiles  
    for seeker in JobSeeker.objects.all():
        seeker.phone = fake.phone_number()
        seeker.address = fake.address()
        # Clear sensitive files
        seeker.resume = None
        seeker.profile_picture = None
        seeker.save()
    
    # Clear job applications to reduce volume size
    JobApplication.objects.filter(
        created_date__lt=timezone.now() - timedelta(days=90)
    ).delete()
    
    print("Development data sanitized successfully")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    sanitize_development_data()

9.5 Disaster Recovery Strategy

Scenario: Multi-region backup and recovery for anihpj

# Comprehensive disaster recovery for anihpj
# Primary region: us-east-1, DR region: us-west-2

# Python script: disaster_recovery_manager.py
import boto3
import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

class AnihpjDisasterRecovery:
    def __init__(self):
        self.primary_region = 'us-east-1'
        self.dr_region = 'us-west-2'
        self.ec2_primary = boto3.client('ec2', region_name=self.primary_region)
        self.ec2_dr = boto3.client('ec2', region_name=self.dr_region)
    
    def create_cross_region_backup(self, volume_id):
        """Create and replicate snapshot to DR region"""
        
        # Create snapshot in primary region
        snapshot_response = self.ec2_primary.create_snapshot(
            VolumeId=volume_id,
            Description=f'anihpj DR backup {datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M")}',
            TagSpecifications=[{
                'ResourceType': 'snapshot',
                'Tags': [
                    {'Key': 'Project', 'Value': 'anihpj'},
                    {'Key': 'BackupType', 'Value': 'disaster-recovery'},
                    {'Key': 'SourceRegion', 'Value': self.primary_region},
                    {'Key': 'CreatedBy', 'Value': 'dr-automation'}
                ]
            }]
        )
        
        snapshot_id = snapshot_response['SnapshotId']
        print(f"Created snapshot {snapshot_id} in {self.primary_region}")
        
        # Wait for snapshot completion
        waiter = self.ec2_primary.get_waiter('snapshot_completed')
        print("Waiting for snapshot to complete...")
        waiter.wait(SnapshotIds=[snapshot_id])
        
        # Copy to DR region with encryption
        copy_response = self.ec2_dr.copy_snapshot(
            SourceRegion=self.primary_region,
            SourceSnapshotId=snapshot_id,
            Description=f'anihpj DR copy from {self.primary_region}',
            Encrypted=True,
            DestinationRegion=self.dr_region,
            TagSpecifications=[{
                'ResourceType': 'snapshot',
                'Tags': [
                    {'Key': 'Project', 'Value': 'anihpj'},
                    {'Key': 'BackupType', 'Value': 'cross-region-copy'},
                    {'Key': 'SourceSnapshot', 'Value': snapshot_id}
                ]
            }]
        )
        
        dr_snapshot_id = copy_response['SnapshotId']
        print(f"Copied to DR region: {dr_snapshot_id}")
        
        return snapshot_id, dr_snapshot_id
    
    def create_recovery_plan(self):
        """Generate detailed recovery plan document"""
        
        recovery_plan = {
            "disaster_recovery_plan": {
                "service": "anihpj Job Portal",
                "rto_target": "4 hours",  # Recovery Time Objective
                "rpo_target": "1 hour",   # Recovery Point Objective
                "primary_region": self.primary_region,
                "dr_region": self.dr_region,
                
                "recovery_steps": [
                    {
                        "step": 1,
                        "action": "Launch EC2 instance in DR region",
                        "command": "aws ec2 run-instances --image-id ami-12345 --instance-type t3.medium --region us-west-2"
                    },
                    {
                        "step": 2, 
                        "action": "Create volume from DR snapshot",
                        "command": "aws ec2 create-volume --snapshot-id snap-dr123 --availability-zone us-west-2a"
                    },
                    {
                        "step": 3,
                        "action": "Attach volume to DR instance", 
                        "command": "aws ec2 attach-volume --volume-id vol-dr123 --instance-id i-dr123 --device /dev/xvdf"
                    },
                    {
                        "step": 4,
                        "action": "Update DNS to point to DR region",
                        "command": "aws route53 change-resource-record-sets --hosted-zone-id Z123 --change-batch file://dns-failover.json"
                    },
                    {
                        "step": 5,
                        "action": "Start application services",
                        "command": "systemctl start postgresql nginx anihpj"
                    }
                ],
                
                "testing_schedule": "Monthly",
                "backup_schedule": "Daily at 03:00 UTC",
                "retention_policy": "30 days primary, 90 days DR"
            }
        }
        
        # Save recovery plan
        with open('anihpj_dr_plan.json', 'w') as f:
            json.dump(recovery_plan, f, indent=2)
        
        return recovery_plan
    
    def test_recovery_procedure(self, snapshot_id):
        """Test recovery by launching temporary DR instance"""
        
        print("🧪 Testing disaster recovery procedure...")
        
        # Create test volume from DR snapshot
        test_volume = self.ec2_dr.create_volume(
            SnapshotId=snapshot_id,
            AvailabilityZone=f'{self.dr_region}a',
            VolumeType='gp3',
            TagSpecifications=[{
                'ResourceType': 'volume',
                'Tags': [{'Key': 'Name', 'Value': 'anihpj-dr-test'}]
            }]
        )
        
        print(f"Created test volume: {test_volume['VolumeId']}")
        
        # Launch minimal test instance
        test_instance = self.ec2_dr.run_instances(
            ImageId='ami-0abcdef1234567890',  # Amazon Linux 2
            InstanceType='t3.micro',
            MinCount=1, MaxCount=1,
            TagSpecifications=[{
                'ResourceType': 'instance', 
                'Tags': [{'Key': 'Name', 'Value': 'anihpj-dr-test'}]
            }]
        )
        
        instance_id = test_instance['Instances'][0]['InstanceId']
        print(f"Launched test instance: {instance_id}")
        
        # Return cleanup information
        return {
            'test_volume_id': test_volume['VolumeId'],
            'test_instance_id': instance_id,
            'cleanup_note': 'Remember to terminate test resources after validation'
        }

# Usage example
dr_manager = AnihpjDisasterRecovery()

# Backup production database volume
primary_snapshot, dr_snapshot = dr_manager.create_cross_region_backup('vol-prod-database')

# Generate recovery documentation
recovery_plan = dr_manager.create_recovery_plan()

# Test recovery (optional)
test_results = dr_manager.test_recovery_procedure(dr_snapshot)

print("Disaster recovery setup complete!")
print(f"Primary snapshot: {primary_snapshot}")
print(f"DR snapshot: {dr_snapshot}")

# Monthly DR cost estimate:
# Cross-region snapshot copy: ~$2/month (40GB × $0.05)
# DR region storage: $2/month (40GB × $0.05)  
# Total DR cost: ~$4/month (20% of primary storage cost)

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

10.1 Common Issues and Solutions

⚠️ Volume Attachment Issues

Problem: EBS volume fails to attach to EC2 instance

Common Causes & Solutions:

  • Different AZ: Volume and instance must be in same Availability Zone
  • Instance State: Instance must be running or stopped (not stopping/starting)
  • Device Name Conflict: Device already in use (/dev/xvdf already attached)
  • IAM Permissions: Missing ec2:AttachVolume permission
  • Volume Limit: Exceeded maximum volumes per instance (typically 40)
# Troubleshoot volume attachment for anihpj
# Step 1: Check volume and instance are in same AZ
aws ec2 describe-volumes --volume-ids vol-0123456789abcdef0 \
    --query 'Volumes[0].[VolumeId,AvailabilityZone,State]' --output table

aws ec2 describe-instances --instance-ids i-0123456789abcdef0 \
    --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].[InstanceId,Placement.AvailabilityZone,State.Name]' --output table

# Step 2: Check current attachments
aws ec2 describe-volumes --volume-ids vol-0123456789abcdef0 \
    --query 'Volumes[0].Attachments'

# Step 3: List all attached volumes to find free device names
lsblk
df -h

# Step 4: Check system messages for attachment errors
sudo dmesg | tail -20
sudo tail -f /var/log/messages

# Step 5: Force detach if volume is stuck
aws ec2 detach-volume --volume-id vol-0123456789abcdef0 --force

# Step 6: Retry attachment with different device name
aws ec2 attach-volume \
    --volume-id vol-0123456789abcdef0 \
    --instance-id i-0123456789abcdef0 \
    --device /dev/xvdg
⚠️ Performance Issues

Problem: Poor I/O performance or high latency on anihpj database

Diagnostic Steps:

  1. Check if instance is EBS-optimized
  2. Monitor queue depth (should be <10)
  3. Verify IOPS provisioning vs actual usage
  4. Check for network bandwidth limits
  5. Review application-level bottlenecks
# Diagnose EBS performance issues for anihpj
# Install performance monitoring tools
sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get install -y iotop sysstat htop

# Monitor real-time I/O performance
sudo iotop -a  # Shows accumulated I/O per process
iostat -x 1    # Extended statistics every second

# Check current queue depth and IOPS
iostat -x 1 | grep xvdf  # Monitor specific EBS volume

# Monitor Django/PostgreSQL processes
sudo htop  # Look for high I/O wait (red bars)

# Check EBS CloudWatch metrics
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EBS \
    --metric-name VolumeQueueLength \
    --dimensions Name=VolumeId,Value=vol-0123456789abcdef0 \
    --start-time 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2024-01-01T23:59:59Z \
    --period 300 \
    --statistics Average,Maximum

# Check if instance is EBS-optimized
aws ec2 describe-instances --instance-ids i-0123456789abcdef0 \
    --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].EbsOptimized'

# Enable EBS optimization if disabled
aws ec2 modify-instance-attribute \
    --instance-id i-0123456789abcdef0 \
    --ebs-optimized

# PostgreSQL-specific performance checks
sudo -u postgres psql -d anihpj_db -c "
    SELECT schemaname,tablename,attname,n_distinct,correlation 
    FROM pg_stats 
    WHERE tablename IN ('jobpost_job', 'auth_user') 
    ORDER BY n_distinct DESC LIMIT 10;"

# Check for missing database indexes
sudo -u postgres psql -d anihpj_db -c "
    SELECT schemaname, tablename, attname, n_distinct, correlation
    FROM pg_stats 
    WHERE tablename = 'jobpost_job' 
    AND correlation < 0.1;"

10.2 Frequently Asked Questions

Q: Can I attach one EBS volume to multiple EC2 instances simultaneously?

A: Only io2 volumes support Multi-Attach (up to 16 instances in same AZ). gp3/gp2 volumes can only attach to one instance at a time. For anihpj, use Amazon RDS for shared database access instead of Multi-Attach.

Q: What happens if my EC2 instance fails? Will I lose my anihpj data?

A: No, EBS volumes persist independently of EC2 instances. You can detach the volume from the failed instance and attach it to a new instance. Always maintain regular snapshots for additional protection.

Q: How do I migrate EBS volumes between Availability Zones for anihpj?

A: Create a snapshot of the volume, then create a new volume from the snapshot in the target AZ. You cannot directly move volumes between AZs. Plan for ~30 minutes downtime for 100GB database volume.

Q: Should I use RAID with EBS volumes for anihpj database performance?

A: Generally no. EBS already provides 99.999% durability. For anihpj, use a single gp3 volume (up to 16,000 IOPS). If you need more performance, consider Amazon RDS Aurora instead of RAID.

Q: How do I resize an EBS volume without downtime for anihpj?

A: Use `aws ec2 modify-volume` to increase size, then `resize2fs` (ext4) or `xfs_growfs` (XFS) to extend the filesystem. No downtime required for size increases. Cannot decrease volume size.

Q: What's the difference between EBS snapshots and AMI backups for anihpj?

A: EBS snapshots backup individual volumes (recommended for data). AMIs create complete instance images including all volumes. For anihpj database protection, use EBS snapshots of the database volume.

Q: Why is my restored EBS volume slower than expected?

A: Volumes restored from snapshots have initialization overhead. Pre-warm by reading all blocks: `sudo dd if=/dev/xvdf of=/dev/null bs=1M`. Consider Fast Snapshot Restore for production workloads ($0.75/snapshot/AZ/month).

Q: How much does EBS cost compared to RDS for anihpj database?

A: EBS + EC2: ~$44/month (t3.medium + 100GB gp3 + snapshots). RDS db.t3.micro: ~$13/month (managed). RDS includes automated backups, patches, Multi-AZ. Choose based on management preference.

Q: Can I encrypt existing unencrypted EBS volumes?

A: Not directly. Create an encrypted snapshot of the unencrypted volume, then create a new encrypted volume from that snapshot. Requires brief downtime to swap volumes.

Q: How do I monitor EBS costs for anihpj across multiple environments?

A: Use Cost Explorer with tags (Project=anihpj, Environment=prod/staging/dev). Set up billing alerts for unexpected costs. Use the cost optimization script provided in Best Practices section.

10.3 Error Messages and Solutions

Error Message Common Cause Solution
InvalidVolume.NotFound Wrong volume ID or region Verify volume ID and current region setting
IncorrectState Volume in transitional state Wait for current operation to complete
InvalidAttachment.NotFound Volume not actually attached Check volume attachment status first
VolumeInUse Volume attached to running instance Stop instance or use force detach
InvalidSnapshot.NotFound Snapshot doesn't exist or no permissions Check snapshot ID and IAM permissions
InvalidDevice.InUse Device name already in use Use different device name (/dev/xvdg, /dev/xvdh)
InvalidParameterValue Invalid IOPS for volume type Check IOPS limits for gp3 (3,000-16,000)
VolumeLimitExceeded Too many volumes per instance Detach unused volumes or use larger volumes

    --destination-region us-west-2 \
    --description "anihpj DR backup from us-east-1" \
    --encrypted

# Delete old snapshots (cleanup script)
aws ec2 describe-snapshots \
    --owner-ids self \
    --filters "Name=tag:Project,Values=anihpj" "Name=tag:RetentionDays,Values=7" \
    --query "Snapshots[?StartTime<='$(date -d '7 days ago' -Iseconds)'].SnapshotId" \
    --output text | xargs -n 1 aws ec2 delete-snapshot --snapshot-id

11.2 Boto3 Python Integration for Django

# anihpj/utils/ebs_manager.py - EBS management utilities
import boto3
import logging
from datetime import datetime, timedelta, timezone
from django.conf import settings
from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand

logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

class AnihpjEBSManager:
    """EBS management utilities for anihpj job portal"""
    
    def __init__(self, region='us-east-1'):
        self.region = region
        self.ec2_client = boto3.client('ec2', region_name=region)
        self.ec2_resource = boto3.resource('ec2', region_name=region)
        self.cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name=region)
    
    def create_database_backup(self, volume_id, retention_days=7):
        """Create encrypted snapshot backup for anihpj database"""
        
        try:
            response = self.ec2_client.create_snapshot(
                VolumeId=volume_id,
                Description=f'anihpj database backup {datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M")}',
                TagSpecifications=[{
                    'ResourceType': 'snapshot',
                    'Tags': [
                        {'Key': 'Project', 'Value': 'anihpj'},
                        {'Key': 'Application', 'Value': 'job-portal'},
                        {'Key': 'VolumeType', 'Value': 'database'},
                        {'Key': 'Environment', 'Value': settings.ENVIRONMENT},
                        {'Key': 'RetentionDays', 'Value': str(retention_days)},
                        {'Key': 'CreatedBy', 'Value': 'django-automation'},
                        {'Key': 'BackupTime', 'Value': datetime.now().isoformat()}
                    ]
                }]
            )
            
            snapshot_id = response['SnapshotId']
            logger.info(f'Created snapshot {snapshot_id} for volume {volume_id}')
            
            # Send notification (integrate with Django messaging or email)
            self._send_backup_notification(snapshot_id, volume_id, success=True)
            
            return snapshot_id
            
        except Exception as e:
            logger.error(f'Failed to create snapshot for {volume_id}: {str(e)}')
            self._send_backup_notification(None, volume_id, success=False, error=str(e))
            raise
    
    def cleanup_old_snapshots(self, retention_days=7):
        """Delete snapshots older than retention period"""
        
        cutoff_date = datetime.now(timezone.utc) - timedelta(days=retention_days)
        
        snapshots = self.ec2_client.describe_snapshots(
            OwnerIds=['self'],
            Filters=[
                {'Name': 'tag:Project', 'Values': ['anihpj']},
                {'Name': 'tag:RetentionDays', 'Values': [str(retention_days)]}
            ]
        )
        
        deleted_count = 0
        freed_storage_gb = 0
        
        for snapshot in snapshots['Snapshots']:
            if snapshot['StartTime'] < cutoff_date:
                try:
                    snapshot_id = snapshot['SnapshotId']
                    volume_size = snapshot['VolumeSize']
                    
                    self.ec2_client.delete_snapshot(SnapshotId=snapshot_id)
                    
                    deleted_count += 1
                    freed_storage_gb += volume_size
                    logger.info(f'Deleted old snapshot {snapshot_id} ({volume_size}GB)')
                    
                except Exception as e:
                    logger.error(f'Failed to delete snapshot {snapshot_id}: {str(e)}')
        
        cost_savings = freed_storage_gb * 0.05  # $0.05 per GB per month
        logger.info(f'Cleanup complete: {deleted_count} snapshots deleted, '
                   f'{freed_storage_gb}GB freed, ${cost_savings:.2f}/month saved')
        
        return {
            'deleted_count': deleted_count,
            'freed_storage_gb': freed_storage_gb,
            'monthly_savings': cost_savings
        }
    
    def get_volume_performance_metrics(self, volume_id, hours=24):
        """Get comprehensive performance metrics for volume"""
        
        end_time = datetime.utcnow()
        start_time = end_time - timedelta(hours=hours)
        
        metrics = {}
        metric_definitions = {
            'VolumeReadOps': 'Read IOPS',
            'VolumeWriteOps': 'Write IOPS', 
            'VolumeReadBytes': 'Read Throughput (Bytes)',
            'VolumeWriteBytes': 'Write Throughput (Bytes)',
            'VolumeQueueLength': 'Queue Depth',
            'VolumeTotalReadTime': 'Read Latency (Seconds)',
            'VolumeTotalWriteTime': 'Write Latency (Seconds)'
        }
        
        for metric_name, description in metric_definitions.items():
            try:
                response = self.cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics(
                    Namespace='AWS/EBS',
                    MetricName=metric_name,
                    Dimensions=[{'Name': 'VolumeId', 'Value': volume_id}],
                    StartTime=start_time,
                    EndTime=end_time,
                    Period=3600,  # 1-hour periods
                    Statistics=['Average', 'Maximum', 'Sum']
                )
                
                datapoints = response['Datapoints']
                if datapoints:
                    metrics[metric_name] = {
                        'description': description,
                        'average': sum(d['Average'] for d in datapoints) / len(datapoints),
                        'maximum': max(d['Maximum'] for d in datapoints),
                        'total': sum(d.get('Sum', d['Average']) for d in datapoints),
                        'datapoint_count': len(datapoints)
                    }
                    
            except Exception as e:
                logger.warning(f'Failed to get {metric_name} for {volume_id}: {str(e)}')
        
        # Calculate derived metrics
        if 'VolumeReadOps' in metrics and 'VolumeWriteOps' in metrics:
            metrics['TotalIOPS'] = {
                'description': 'Total IOPS (Read + Write)',
                'average': metrics['VolumeReadOps']['average'] + metrics['VolumeWriteOps']['average'],
                'maximum': metrics['VolumeReadOps']['maximum'] + metrics['VolumeWriteOps']['maximum']
            }
        
        return metrics
    
    def _send_backup_notification(self, snapshot_id, volume_id, success=True, error=None):
        """Send backup notification (integrate with your notification system)"""
        
        if success:
            message = f'✅ anihpj database backup successful: {snapshot_id}'
        else:
            message = f'❌ anihpj database backup failed for {volume_id}: {error}'
        
        # Log for now - integrate with Django messages, email, or Slack
        logger.info(f'Backup notification: {message}')
        
        # Example integration with Django admin messages
        # from django.contrib import messages
        # messages.success(request, message) if success else messages.error(request, message)

11.3 Django Management Commands

# anihpj/management/commands/ebs_backup.py
from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand, CommandError
from django.conf import settings
from anihpj.utils.ebs_manager import AnihpjEBSManager
import os

class Command(BaseCommand):
    help = 'Create EBS snapshot backup of anihpj database volume'
    
    def add_arguments(self, parser):
        parser.add_argument(
            '--volume-id',
            type=str,
            default=os.environ.get('ANIHPJ_DB_VOLUME_ID'),
            help='EBS volume ID to backup (default: from ANIHPJ_DB_VOLUME_ID env var)'
        )
        parser.add_argument(
            '--retention-days',
            type=int,
            default=7,
            help='Number of days to retain snapshots (default: 7)'
        )
        parser.add_argument(
            '--cleanup',
            action='store_true',
            help='Also cleanup old snapshots beyond retention period'
        )
        parser.add_argument(
            '--performance-report',
            action='store_true', 
            help='Generate performance report for the volume'
        )
    
    def handle(self, *args, **options):
        if not options['volume_id']:
            raise CommandError('Volume ID is required. Set ANIHPJ_DB_VOLUME_ID or use --volume-id')
        
        ebs_manager = AnihpjEBSManager()
        volume_id = options['volume_id']
        
        self.stdout.write(f'Processing volume: {volume_id}')
        
        # Create backup
        try:
            snapshot_id = ebs_manager.create_database_backup(
                volume_id, 
                retention_days=options['retention_days']
            )
            self.stdout.write(
                self.style.SUCCESS(f'✅ Backup created: {snapshot_id}')
            )
        except Exception as e:
            raise CommandError(f'Backup failed: {str(e)}')
        
        # Cleanup old snapshots if requested
        if options['cleanup']:
            try:
                cleanup_results = ebs_manager.cleanup_old_snapshots(
                    retention_days=options['retention_days']
                )
                self.stdout.write(
                    self.style.SUCCESS(
                        f'🗑️  Cleanup: {cleanup_results["deleted_count"]} snapshots deleted, '
                        f'${cleanup_results["monthly_savings"]:.2f}/month saved'
                    )
                )
            except Exception as e:
                self.stdout.write(
                    self.style.ERROR(f'Cleanup failed: {str(e)}')
                )
        
        # Generate performance report if requested
        if options['performance_report']:
            try:
                metrics = ebs_manager.get_volume_performance_metrics(volume_id, hours=24)
                
                self.stdout.write('\n📊 24-Hour Performance Report:')
                self.stdout.write('-' * 50)
                
                for metric_name, data in metrics.items():
                    if isinstance(data, dict) and 'description' in data:
                        self.stdout.write(
                            f"{data['description']}: "
                            f"Avg={data['average']:.2f}, Max={data['maximum']:.2f}"
                        )
                
                # Performance recommendations
                if 'VolumeQueueLength' in metrics:
                    avg_queue = metrics['VolumeQueueLength']['average']
                    if avg_queue > 10:
                        self.stdout.write(
                            self.style.WARNING(
                                f'⚠️  High queue depth ({avg_queue:.1f}): Consider upgrading to io2 or EBS-optimized instance'
                            )
                        )
                
            except Exception as e:
                self.stdout.write(
                    self.style.ERROR(f'Performance report failed: {str(e)}')
                )

# Usage examples:
# python manage.py ebs_backup --volume-id vol-0123456789abcdef0
# python manage.py ebs_backup --cleanup --performance-report
# python manage.py ebs_backup --retention-days 14 --cleanup

# Launch EBS-optimized EC2 instance for anihpj with proper configuration
aws ec2 run-instances \

    --instance-type t3.medium \
    --key-name anihpj-keypair \

        {Key=Name,Value=anihpj-app-server},

    --user-data file://anihpj-userdata.sh

# anihpj-userdata.sh - Automated EBS setup script
#!/bin/bash
set -e

# Update system and install required packages
yum update -y
yum install -y postgresql14-server nginx python3 python3-pip

# Install CloudWatch agent for monitoring
yum install -y amazon-cloudwatch-agent

# Wait for EBS volumes to be attached
echo "Waiting for EBS volumes..."
while [ ! -e /dev/xvdf ]; do sleep 2; done  # Database volume
while [ ! -e /dev/xvdg ]; do sleep 2; done  # Logs volume

# Setup database volume (/dev/xvdf)
echo "Setting up database volume..."
mkfs.ext4 /dev/xvdf
mkdir -p /var/lib/postgresql/data
mount /dev/xvdf /var/lib/postgresql/data
echo '/dev/xvdf /var/lib/postgresql/data ext4 defaults,nofail 0 2' >> /etc/fstab

# Setup logs volume (/dev/xvdg)  
echo "Setting up logs volume..."
mkfs.ext4 /dev/xvdg
mkdir -p /var/log/anihpj
mount /dev/xvdg /var/log/anihpj
echo '/dev/xvdg /var/log/anihpj ext4 defaults,nofail 0 2' >> /etc/fstab

# Set proper ownership and permissions
chown -R postgres:postgres /var/lib/postgresql/data
chmod 700 /var/lib/postgresql/data
chown -R www-data:www-data /var/log/anihpj
chmod 755 /var/log/anihpj

# Initialize PostgreSQL
sudo -u postgres initdb -D /var/lib/postgresql/data
systemctl enable postgresql
systemctl start postgresql

# Install and configure anihpj application
cd /opt
git clone https://github.com/your-org/anihpj.git
cd anihpj
pip3 install -r requirements.txt

# Setup Django environment
python3 manage.py migrate
python3 manage.py collectstatic --noinput

# Start services
systemctl enable nginx
systemctl start nginx

echo "anihpj server setup complete!"
💡 EBS-Optimized Instance Benefits for anihpj
  • Dedicated Bandwidth: Separate network path for EBS traffic (500 Mbps for t3.medium)
  • Consistent Performance: No competition between application traffic and storage I/O
  • Higher IOPS: Better throughput for PostgreSQL database operations
  • Minimal Cost Increase: ~10% premium (t3.medium: $30 → $33/month)
  • Lower Latency: Reduced I/O latency for Django application responses

12.2 RDS Integration: Hybrid Architecture

Combine EBS and RDS for optimal anihpj architecture:

Component EBS-Only Architecture Hybrid EBS + RDS Recommendation
Database PostgreSQL on EBS ($16/month) RDS PostgreSQL ($13/month) ✅ RDS for managed database
Application Files EBS volumes ($8/month) EBS volumes ($8/month) ✅ Keep on EBS for flexibility
Backups Manual snapshots Automated RDS backups ✅ RDS automated backups
High Availability Manual snapshot recovery RDS Multi-AZ ✅ RDS Multi-AZ for HA
Management Overhead High (patches, backups, monitoring) Low (AWS managed) ✅ Reduced operational burden 
# Hybrid architecture: RDS for database + EBS for application storage
# Create RDS instance for anihpj database
aws rds create-db-instance \
    --db-instance-identifier anihpj-database \
    --db-instance-class db.t3.micro \
    --engine postgres \
    --engine-version 14.9 \
    --allocated-storage 100 \
    --storage-type gp3 \
    --storage-encrypted \
    --multi-az \
    --backup-retention-period 30 \
    --preferred-backup-window "03:00-04:00" \
    --preferred-maintenance-window "sun:04:00-sun:05:00" \
    --db-name anihpj_db \
    --master-username anihpj_admin \
    --master-user-password "$(aws secretsmanager get-secret-value --secret-id anihpj/db/password --query SecretString --output text)" \
    --vpc-security-group-ids sg-0123456789abcdef0 \
    --db-subnet-group-name anihpj-db-subnet-group \
    --tags Key=Project,Value=anihpj Key=Environment,Value=production

# EBS volumes for application data (not database)
# Media files volume
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 50 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --encrypted \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[
        {Key=Name,Value=anihpj-media},
        {Key=Project,Value=anihpj},
        {Key=Purpose,Value=django-media}
    ]'

# Application logs volume  
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 30 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[
        {Key=Name,Value=anihpj-logs},
        {Key=Project,Value=anihpj}
    ]'

# Updated Django settings for hybrid architecture
